import tarfile, pathlib, os
path='/mnt/data/polylogue-all.tar(78).gz'
dest=pathlib.Path('/mnt/data/polylogue_extract').resolve()
with tarfile.open(path,'r:gz') as t:
    for m in t.getmembers():
        target=(dest/m.name).resolve()
        if not str(target).startswith(str(dest)+os.sep):
            raise Exception('unsafe path '+m.name)
    t.extractall(dest)
print('extracted')

import json
p='polylogue-beads.json'
data=json.load(open(p))
print(type(data))
if isinstance(data, dict):
    print(data.keys())
    for k,v in data.items():
        print(k, type(v), len(v) if hasattr(v,'__len__') else '')
        if isinstance(v, list) and v:
            print('first', v[0].keys() if isinstance(v[0], dict) else type(v[0]), v[0] if not isinstance(v[0], dict) else {kk:v[0][kk] for kk in list(v[0])[:10]})
        if isinstance(v, dict):
            print('dict keys', list(v)[:20])
else:
    print(len(data)); print(data[0])

## 37. assistant

_create_time: 1783375451.548299_

bash -lc cd /mnt/data/polylogue_extract/polylogue && python3 - <<'PY'
import json, collections
issues=[]
for line in open('polylogue-beads-export.jsonl'):
    obj=json.loads(line)
    if obj.get('_type')=='issue': issues.append(obj)
print('issues', len(issues))
status=collections.Counter(i['status'] for i in issues)
itype=collections.Counter(i['issue_type'] for i in issues)
print('status',status)
print('types',itype)
# deps from export and json
deps=[]
for i in issues:
    for d in i.get('dependencies',[]) or []:
        deps.append((d['issue_id'], d['depends_on_id'], d.get('type')))
print('deps export', len(deps), collections.Counter(t for _,_,t in deps))
# top open with dependency count etc
open_issues=[i for i in issues if i['status']!='closed']
print('open',len(open_issues),collections.Counter(i['status'] for i in open_issues))
print('open dep types touching')
# Counts of deps for open issue and blockers open/closed
ids={i['id']:i for i in issues}
for t in sorted(set(t for _,_,t in deps)):
    n=sum(1 for issue,dep,tt in deps if tt==t and ids[issue]['status']!='closed')
    n_open_dep=sum(1 for issue,dep,tt in deps if tt==t and ids[issue]['status']!='closed' and ids.get(dep,{}).get('status')!='closed')
    print(t,n,n_open_dep)
# blocking type only likely 'blocks'
blocked=[]
for i in open_issues:
    bl=[d for d in i.get('dependencies',[]) or [] if d.get('type')=='blocks' and ids.get(d['depends_on_id'],{}).get('status')!='closed']
    if bl: blocked.append(i['id'])
print('open blocked by open blocks',len(blocked),blocked[:20])
# Ready if no open blocks? count
ready=[i['id'] for i in open_issues if not [d for d in i.get('dependencies',[]) or [] if d.get('type')=='blocks' and ids.get(d['depends_on_id'],{}).get('status')!='closed']]
print('ready by open blocks', len(ready), ready[:20])
# Compare blocked_ids JSON
j=json.load(open('polylogue-beads.json'))
print('blocked_ids minus calc', sorted(set(j['blocked_ids'])-set(blocked))[:20], len(set(j['blocked_ids'])-set(blocked)))
print('calc minus blocked_ids', sorted(set(blocked)-set(j['blocked_ids']))[:20], len(set(blocked)-set(j['blocked_ids'])))
print('readyids subset calc?', set(j['ready_ids']).issubset(set(ready)), 'json ready not in calc', sorted(set(j['ready_ids'])-set(ready))[:10])
print('calc ready not json first', sorted(set(ready)-set(j['ready_ids']))[:20], len(set(ready)-set(j['ready_ids'])))
PY

## 59. assistant

_create_time: 1783375526.639103_

bash -lc cd /mnt/data/polylogue_extract/polylogue && python3 - <<'PY'
import json, collections
issues=[]
for line in open('polylogue-beads-export.jsonl'):
 obj=json.loads(line)
 if obj.get('_type')=='issue': issues.append(obj)
ids={i['id']:i for i in issues}
open_ids={i['id'] for i in issues if i['status']!='closed'}
parent={}
for i in issues:
 for d in i.get('dependencies',[]) or []:
  if d.get('type')=='parent-child':
   parent[i['id']]=d['depends_on_id']
# direct open blockers
blocked_by={iid:set() for iid in open_ids}
for i in issues:
 if i['id'] not in open_ids: continue
 for d in i.get('dependencies',[]) or []:
  if d.get('type')=='blocks' and d['depends_on_id'] in open_ids:
   blocked_by[i['id']].add(d['depends_on_id'])
# inherited parent blockers
inherited={iid:set(bs) for iid,bs in blocked_by.items()}
for iid in list(open_ids):
 p=parent.get(iid)
 seen=set()
 while p and p not in seen:
  seen.add(p)
  inherited[iid].update(blocked_by.get(p,set()))
  p=parent.get(p)
blocked=[iid for iid,b in inherited.items() if b]
print('blocked inherited',len(blocked))
j=json.load(open('polylogue-beads.json'))
print('json blocked len',len(j['blocked_ids']))
print('json-blocked minus inherited',sorted(set(j['blocked_ids'])-set(blocked)), len(set(j['blocked_ids'])-set(blocked)))
print('inherited minus json', sorted(set(blocked)-set(j['blocked_ids']))[:50], len(set(blocked)-set(j['blocked_ids'])))
print('ready inherited', len(open_ids)-len(blocked))
PY

## 62. assistant

_create_time: 1783375543.993508_

bash -lc cd /mnt/data/polylogue_extract/polylogue && python3 - <<'PY'
import json, collections, heapq, re
issues=[]
for line in open('polylogue-beads-export.jsonl'):
 obj=json.loads(line)
 if obj.get('_type')=='issue': issues.append(obj)
ids={i['id']:i for i in issues}
open_items=[i for i in issues if i['status']!='closed']
open_ids={i['id'] for i in open_items}
parent={}
children=collections.defaultdict(list)
for i in issues:
 for d in i.get('dependencies',[]) or []:
  if d.get('type')=='parent-child':
   parent[i['id']]=d['depends_on_id']
   children[d['depends_on_id']].append(i['id'])
# hard blocks direct+inherit parent blockers
blocked_by={iid:set() for iid in open_ids}
for i in open_items:
 for d in i.get('dependencies',[]) or []:
  if d.get('type')=='blocks' and d['depends_on_id'] in open_ids:
   blocked_by[i['id']].add(d['depends_on_id'])
# add inherited blockers from ancestor parents
for iid in list(open_ids):
 p=parent.get(iid)
 seen=set()
 while p and p not in seen:
  seen.add(p)
  blocked_by[iid].update(blocked_by.get(p,set()))
  p=parent.get(p)
# topological levels recursively: level=1+max(blockers)
from functools import lru_cache
@lru_cache(None)
def level(iid):
 if not blocked_by[iid]: return 0
 return 1+max(level(b) for b in blocked_by[iid] if b in open_ids)
levels=collections.defaultdict(list)
for i in open_items:
 levels[level(i['id'])].append(i['id'])
print('max level', max(levels), 'levels counts', {k:len(v) for k,v in sorted(levels.items())})
for k in sorted(levels):
 print('\nLEVEL',k)
 for iid in sorted(levels[k], key=lambda x:(ids[x]['priority'], ids[x]['issue_type']!='bug', ids[x]['id']))[:30]:
  print(iid,'P'+str(ids[iid]['priority']),ids[iid]['issue_type'],ids[iid]['status'],ids[iid]['title'][:60], 'blockers:', sorted(blocked_by[iid]))
PY

bash -lc cd /mnt/data/polylogue_extract/polylogue && python3 - <<'PY'
import json, collections, textwrap
issues=[]
for line in open('polylogue-beads-export.jsonl'):
 obj=json.loads(line)
 if obj.get('_type')=='issue': issues.append(obj)
ids={i['id']:i for i in issues}
open_ids={i['id'] for i in issues if i['status']!='closed'}
parent={}
children=collections.defaultdict(list)
for i in issues:
 for d in i.get('dependencies',[]) or []:
  if d.get('type')=='parent-child':
   parent[i['id']]=d['depends_on_id']; children[d['depends_on_id']].append(i['id'])
def root(iid):
 seen=set(); cur=iid
 while parent.get(cur) and parent[cur] in ids and parent[cur] not in seen:
  seen.add(cur); cur=parent[cur]
 return cur
roots=collections.defaultdict(list)
for iid in open_ids:
 roots[root(iid)].append(iid)
# sort by P min and size
items=[]
for r,lst in roots.items():
 if r not in ids: continue
 title=ids[r]['title']; typ=ids[r]['issue_type']; status=ids[r]['status']; pri=ids[r]['priority']
 items.append((pri, -len(lst), r, typ, status, title, len(lst)))
for item in sorted(items)[:80]:
 pri, neg, r, typ, status, title, n=item
 print(f"P{pri} {r} {typ} {status} n={n}: {title}")
PY

bash -lc cd /mnt/data/polylogue_extract/polylogue && python3 - <<'PY'
import json, collections, textwrap
issues=[]
for line in open('polylogue-beads-export.jsonl'):
 obj=json.loads(line)
 if obj.get('_type')=='issue': issues.append(obj)
ids={i['id']:i for i in issues}
open_ids={i['id'] for i in issues if i['status']!='closed'}
parent={}
children=collections.defaultdict(list)
for i in issues:
 for d in i.get('dependencies',[]) or []:
  if d.get('type')=='parent-child': parent[i['id']]=d['depends_on_id']; children[d['depends_on_id']].append(i['id'])
def root(iid):
 seen=set(); cur=iid
 while parent.get(cur) and parent[cur] in ids and parent[cur] not in seen:
  seen.add(cur); cur=parent[cur]
 return cur
roots=collections.defaultdict(list)
for iid in open_ids: roots[root(iid)].append(iid)
# Print root epics/features with children titles (open only)
for r,lst in sorted(roots.items(), key=lambda kv:(ids[kv[0]]['priority'] if kv[0] in ids else 99, ids[kv[0]]['id'] if kv[0] in ids else kv[0])):
 i=ids[r]
 if len(lst)>=4 or i['issue_type']=='epic':
  print('\n###',r,'P'+str(i['priority']),i['issue_type'],i['status'],i['title'])
  desc=(i.get('description') or '').replace('\n',' ')
  print('DESC', desc[:400])
  # top-level open descendants excluding root sorted priority/id
  descs=[iid for iid in lst if iid!=r]
  for iid in sorted(descs, key=lambda x:(ids[x]['priority'],x))[:20]:
   ci=ids[iid]
   print(' -',iid,'P'+str(ci['priority']),ci['issue_type'],ci['status'],ci['title'])

## 83. assistant

_create_time: 1783375640.363382_

bash -lc cat > /mnt/data/make_beads_plan.py <<'PY'
import json
import re
import textwrap
from collections import defaultdict, Counter
from functools import lru_cache
from pathlib import Path

BASE = Path('/mnt/data/polylogue_extract/polylogue')
EXPORT = BASE / 'polylogue-beads-export.jsonl'
BEADS_JSON = BASE / 'polylogue-beads.json'
OUT_MD = Path('/mnt/data/polylogue_beads_execution_plan.md')
OUT_JSON = Path('/mnt/data/polylogue_beads_execution_order.json')

issues = []
for line in EXPORT.read_text(encoding='utf-8').splitlines():
    if not line.strip():
        continue
    obj = json.loads(line)
    if obj.get('_type') == 'issue':
        issues.append(obj)

ids = {i['id']: i for i in issues}
nonclosed = [i for i in issues if i.get('status') != 'closed']
nonclosed_ids = {i['id'] for i in nonclosed}
closed = [i for i in issues if i.get('status') == 'closed']

parent = {}
children = defaultdict(list)
direct_blocks = defaultdict(set)
related = defaultdict(list)
for i in issues:
    iid = i['id']
    for d in i.get('dependencies', []) or []:
        typ = d.get('type')
        dep = d.get('depends_on_id')
        if typ == 'parent-child':
            parent[iid] = dep
            children[dep].append(iid)
        elif typ == 'blocks':
            # only open/in_progress blockers constrain future execution; closed blockers are already satisfied
            if iid in nonclosed_ids and dep in nonclosed_ids:
                direct_blocks[iid].add(dep)
        elif typ in {'related', 'relates-to', 'discovered-from', 'supersedes'}:
            related[iid].append({'type': typ, 'id': dep})

# Hard blockers = direct open blocks + direct blockers of any open ancestor parent.
# This reproduces the 83 explicit blocked_ids from the Beads snapshot.
hard_blockers = {iid: set(direct_blocks.get(iid, set())) for iid in nonclosed_ids}
for iid in list(nonclosed_ids):
    p = parent.get(iid)
    seen = set()
    while p and p in ids and p not in seen:
        seen.add(p)
        hard_blockers[iid].update(direct_blocks.get(p, set()))
        p = parent.get(p)

# Validate no cycles in hard graph and compute wave levels.
visiting = set()
visited = set()
stack = []
cycles = []

@lru_cache(None)
def wave(iid: str) -> int:
    if iid in visiting:
        cycles.append(stack[stack.index(iid):] + [iid] if iid in stack else [iid])
        return 0
    if iid in visited:
        return 0 if not hard_blockers[iid] else 1 + max(wave(b) for b in hard_blockers[iid] if b in nonclosed_ids)
    visiting.add(iid)
    stack.append(iid)
    blockers = [b for b in hard_blockers[iid] if b in nonclosed_ids]
    value = 0 if not blockers else 1 + max(wave(b) for b in blockers)
    stack.pop()
    visiting.remove(iid)
    visited.add(iid)
    return value

for iid in nonclosed_ids:
    wave(iid)

# Root hierarchy helpers.
def root_of(iid: str) -> str:
    seen = set()
    cur = iid
    while parent.get(cur) and parent[cur] in ids and parent[cur] not in seen:
        seen.add(cur)
        cur = parent[cur]
    return cur

def ancestry(iid: str) -> list[str]:
    out = []
    seen = set()
    cur = iid
    while parent.get(cur) and parent[cur] in ids and parent[cur] not in seen:
        p = parent[cur]
        out.append(p)
        seen.add(p)
        cur = p
    return out

# Descendant count for container notes.
def descendants(iid: str) -> list[str]:
    out = []
    stack2 = list(children.get(iid, []))
    seen = set()
    while stack2:
        c = stack2.pop()
        if c in seen:
            continue
        seen.add(c)
        out.append(c)
        stack2.extend(children.get(c, []))
    return out

TYPE_ORDER = {'bug': 0, 'task': 1, 'feature': 2, 'decision': 3, 'chore': 4, 'epic': 5}
STATUS_ORDER = {'in_progress': 0, 'open': 1}

def natural_key(s: str):
    return [int(part) if part.isdigit() else part for part in re.split(r'(\d+)', s)]

def sort_key(i):
    iid = i['id']
    root = root_of(iid)
    return (
        wave(iid),
        int(i.get('priority', 9)),
        STATUS_ORDER.get(i.get('status'), 9),
        TYPE_ORDER.get(i.get('issue_type'), 9),
        natural_key(root),
        natural_key(iid),
    )

ordered = sorted(nonclosed, key=sort_key)
order_index = {i['id']: n + 1 for n, i in enumerate(ordered)}

# Unlocks by direct hard blocker (including inherited edges, for schedule-level unlocks)
unlocks = defaultdict(list)
for iid, blockers in hard_blockers.items():
    for b in blockers:
        if b in nonclosed_ids:
            unlocks[b].append(iid)

# short, non-invasive text helpers.
def one_line(text: object, *, max_len: int = 260) -> str:
    if text is None:
        return ''
    s = str(text).strip().replace('\r\n', '\n').replace('\r', '\n')
    s = re.sub(r'\s+', ' ', s)
    if len(s) > max_len:
        s = s[: max_len - 1].rstrip() + '…'
    return s

def detail_for(i) -> str:
    # Prefer acceptance/design/description in that order when present; these explain what execution means.
    for field in ('acceptance_criteria', 'design', 'description', 'notes'):
        val = one_line(i.get(field), max_len=300)
        if val:
            return val
    return one_line(i.get('title'), max_len=300)

beads_json = json.loads(BEADS_JSON.read_text(encoding='utf-8'))
summary = beads_json.get('summary', {})
counts = beads_json.get('counts', {})
blocked_ids_export = set(beads_json.get('blocked_ids', []))

# Machine-readable data.
rows = []
for i in ordered:
    iid = i['id']
    root = root_of(iid)
    row = {
        'order': order_index[iid],
        'wave': wave(iid),
        'id': iid,
        'priority': i.get('priority'),
        'status': i.get('status'),
        'type': i.get('issue_type'),
        'title': i.get('title'),
        'root_id': root,
        'root_title': ids[root].get('title') if root in ids else None,
        'hard_prerequisites': sorted(hard_blockers[iid], key=natural_key),
        'direct_blockers': sorted(direct_blocks.get(iid, []), key=natural_key),
        'inherited_blockers': sorted(hard_blockers[iid] - direct_blocks.get(iid, set()), key=natural_key),
        'parent_chain': ancestry(iid),
        'description': detail_for(i),
        'labels': i.get('labels', []),
        'unlocks': sorted(unlocks.get(iid, []), key=natural_key),
    }
    rows.append(row)

OUT_JSON.write_text(json.dumps({
    'source': str(EXPORT),
    'generated_from_snapshot': beads_json.get('generated_at'),
    'ordering_rules': [
        'closed issues are treated as already complete and omitted from execution order',
        'hard prerequisites are non-closed blocks dependencies',
        'a child inherits blockers from its parent chain; this reproduces the snapshot blocked_ids list',
        'parent-child edges group work and define container closure, but are not themselves blockers',
        'within each wave the stable tie-break is priority, status, type, root id, issue id',
    ],
    'counts': {
        'total_issues': len(issues),
        'closed_issues': len(closed),
        'nonclosed_issues_in_plan': len(nonclosed),
        'status': Counter(i.get('status') for i in issues),
        'type': Counter(i.get('issue_type') for i in issues),
        'direct_open_blocked_nonclosed': sum(1 for iid in nonclosed_ids if direct_blocks.get(iid)),
        'inherited_blocked_nonclosed': sum(1 for iid in nonclosed_ids if hard_blockers.get(iid)),
        'waves': Counter(wave(i['id']) for i in nonclosed),
        'beads_summary': summary,
        'beads_counts': counts,
    },
    'cycles': cycles,
    'rows': rows,
}, indent=2, ensure_ascii=False), encoding='utf-8')

# Human-readable report.
lines = []
lines.append('# Polylogue Beads execution plan')
lines.append('')
lines.append(f'Snapshot: `{beads_json.get("generated_at")}` from `{BEADS_JSON.name}` and `{EXPORT.name}`.')
lines.append('')
lines.append('## Interpretation')
lines.append('')
lines.append('This plan orders the non-closed Beads. Closed Beads are already satisfied and are therefore excluded from the execution queue. A hard prerequisite is a non-closed `blocks` dependency. A child also inherits the hard blockers of its parent chain; that rule exactly reproduces the 83 `blocked_ids` in the snapshot. `parent-child` edges are used for hierarchy and final container closure, not as direct execution blockers.')
lines.append('')
lines.append('Within the same dependency wave, the tie-break is: priority, in-progress before open, issue type (`bug`, `task`, `feature`, `decision`, `chore`, `epic`), root id, then issue id.')
lines.append('')
lines.append('## Counts')
lines.append('')
lines.append('| Signal | Count |')
lines.append('| --- | ---: |')
lines.append(f'| Total Beads in export | {len(issues)} |')
lines.append(f'| Already closed | {len(closed)} |')
lines.append(f'| In execution plan | {len(nonclosed)} |')
for st, cnt in sorted(Counter(i.get('status') for i in nonclosed).items()):
    lines.append(f'| Non-closed status: `{st}` | {cnt} |')
for typ, cnt in sorted(Counter(i.get('issue_type') for i in nonclosed).items()):
    lines.append(f'| Non-closed type: `{typ}` | {cnt} |')
lines.append(f'| Directly blocked by open/in-progress blockers | {sum(1 for iid in nonclosed_ids if direct_blocks.get(iid))} |')
lines.append(f'| Blocked after parent-blocker propagation | {sum(1 for iid in nonclosed_ids if hard_blockers.get(iid))} |')
for w, cnt in sorted(Counter(wave(i['id']) for i in nonclosed).items()):
    name = 'now' if w == 0 else f'after wave {w-1}'
    lines.append(f'| Wave {w} ({name}) | {cnt} |')
lines.append('')
if cycles:
    lines.append('Hard dependency cycles detected:')
    for cyc in cycles:
        lines.append('- ' + ' -> '.join(cyc))
else:
    lines.append('No hard dependency cycles were detected.')
lines.append('')

# Top-level programs/end-state organizing map.
root_groups = defaultdict(list)
for i in nonclosed:
    root_groups[root_of(i['id'])].append(i['id'])
lines.append('## Program map')
lines.append('')
lines.append('| Root bead | P | Type | Non-closed descendants incl. root | Meaning |')
lines.append('| --- | ---: | --- | ---: | --- |')
for root, members in sorted(root_groups.items(), key=lambda kv: (ids[kv[0]].get('priority', 9), -len(kv[1]), natural_key(kv[0]))):
    ri = ids[root]
    if len(members) >= 2 or ri.get('issue_type') == 'epic':
        lines.append(f'| `{root}` | {ri.get("priority")} | `{ri.get("issue_type")}` | {len(members)} | {one_line(ri.get("title"), max_len=160)} |')
lines.append('')

# ordered rows by wave.
lines.append('## Full execution order')
lines.append('')
for w in sorted(Counter(wave(i['id']) for i in nonclosed)):
    wave_items = [i for i in ordered if wave(i['id']) == w]
    title = 'Wave 0 — executable now' if w == 0 else f'Wave {w} — unlocked after all listed earlier-wave prerequisites close'
    lines.append(f'### {title}')
    lines.append('')
    for i in wave_items:
        iid = i['id']
        root = root_of(iid)
        marker = 'container' if i.get('issue_type') == 'epic' else 'work'
        prereq = sorted(hard_blockers[iid], key=natural_key)
        if prereq:
            prereq_text = ', '.join(f'`{b}`' for b in prereq)
        else:
            prereq_text = 'none'
        direct = sorted(direct_blocks.get(iid, []), key=natural_key)
        inherited = sorted(hard_blockers[iid] - direct_blocks.get(iid, set()), key=natural_key)
        suffix = ''
        if direct and inherited:
            suffix = f' Direct blockers: {", ".join(f"`{b}`" for b in direct)}. Inherited through parent: {", ".join(f"`{b}`" for b in inherited)}.'
        elif inherited:
            suffix = f' Inherited through parent: {", ".join(f"`{b}`" for b in inherited)}.'
        lines.append(f'{order_index[iid]}. `{iid}` — P{i.get("priority")} `{i.get("status")}` `{i.get("issue_type")}` ({marker})')
        lines.append(f'   Title: {one_line(i.get("title"), max_len=260)}')
        lines.append(f'   Root: `{root}` — {one_line(ids[root].get("title"), max_len=220)}')
        lines.append(f'   Prerequisites: {prereq_text}.{suffix}')
        if i.get('issue_type') == 'epic':
            open_desc = [d for d in descendants(iid) if d in nonclosed_ids]
            lines.append(f'   Execution meaning: keep this container open while its {len(open_desc)} non-closed descendant bead(s) execute; close it when the program acceptance is met.')
        lines.append(f'   Description: {detail_for(i)}')
        if unlocks.get(iid):
            u = sorted(unlocks[iid], key=natural_key)
            shown = ', '.join(f'`{x}`' for x in u[:16])
            if len(u) > 16:
                shown += f', … +{len(u)-16} more'
            lines.append(f'   Unlocks: {shown}.')
        lines.append('')

lines.append('## Precise end state after the plan is fully executed')
lines.append('')
lines.append('At the tracker level, every non-closed bead in this snapshot is closed: 397 currently non-closed beads move to `closed`, leaving 492 closed Beads total, no `open`, no `in_progress`, no ready queue, and no blocked queue. All 623 exported dependency edges are either satisfied closure history, hierarchy, or non-blocking relation metadata.')
lines.append('')
lines.append('At the system level, Polylogue is the local system of record for AI work. Source acquisition, provider/origin identity, parsing, storage, lineage, blobs, assertions, preferences, derived read models, query, rendering, MCP, CLI, daemon, web workbench, docs, and release artifacts all converge on one evidence-backed archive substrate rather than parallel surface-specific implementations.')
lines.append('')
lines.append('The durable archive contains honest source rows, logical sessions, messages, blocks, actions, files, attachments, blobs, assertions, user preferences, ops metadata, hook/OTLP events, agent identity, and work graph units. Attachments have acquired bytes where possible or explicit acquisition status where impossible; blob hashes are honest rather than synthetic; garbage collection is lease-safe; backups restore; deleted/secret material can be excised; zstd compression keeps blob storage affordable.')
lines.append('')
lines.append('Lineage is truthful: fork/resume/compaction share content without double counting; logical-session composition is complete or explicitly marked incomplete; compaction has boundary ranges, effective-context derivation, pre-compaction snapshots, loss-forensics tables, and re-grounding surfaces. Physical source identity stays distinct beneath public origin collapse.')
lines.append('')
lines.append('Derived models are declared and rebuildable: session profiles, work events, phases, threads, delegations, episodes, turn pairs, artifact edges, citation anchors, analyses, findings, result sets, measurement registries, activity spans, embeddings, and retrieval bands all carry provenance, uncertainty, freshness, and degraded-state evidence. Silent soft failure is replaced with explicit degraded modes.')
lines.append('')
lines.append('The query/read contract is unified: one grammar and one Query × Projection × Render algebra drive CLI, MCP, Python API, daemon, web reader, exports, compacted projections, aggregates, sets, pipelines, preferences, and learned defaults. Public surfaces use origin vocabulary rather than leaking provider-wire tokens; surface math is pulled into insights/API contracts; dead or zero-use commands/tools are pruned or adopted.')
lines.append('')
lines.append('Agent coordination is operational: one-command hooks, MCP write access, role-aware mutation safety, coordination messages, scheduler advisories, blackboard-style cross-session messages, handoffs, postmortem bundles, PR provenance, and live multi-agent proof all work across separate worktrees. Beads is an adapter, not a hard dependency; GitHub/git/session inference still gives evidence when Beads is absent.')
lines.append('')
lines.append('Content variants are first-class: language detection and preferences choose variants; original and transformed objects are stored as aligned variant nodes with refs; query, reader, export, review, and messaging surfaces can use translations or other transformed forms without mistaking them for original evidence.')
lines.append('')
lines.append('The operator-facing product is fast and legible: CLI cold/hot paths route through the daemon when available, result caches and push channels serve interactive UIs, webui v2 provides an evidence cockpit and timeline/firehose, release/install/docs claims have executable evidence, public demos are construct-valid, and the docs site makes the system understandable to a stranger.')

OUT_MD.write_text('\n'.join(lines) + '\n', encoding='utf-8')
print(OUT_MD, OUT_MD.stat().st_size)
print(OUT_JSON, OUT_JSON.stat().st_size)

## 94. assistant

_create_time: 1783376161.068284_

I treated “beads” as the Beads issue records in the archive. Closed beads are already executed, so the execution plan covers the 397 still-active beads: 396 open plus 1 in progress. I generated a full ordered execution table with every bead, its priority/type/status, parent bead, hard prerequisites, intent, and done state:

[Full Beads execution order — Markdown](sandbox:/mnt/data/polylogue_beads_execution_order.md)  
[Full Beads execution order — CSV](sandbox:/mnt/data/polylogue_beads_execution_order.csv)

The ordering rule I used is: finish hard `blocks` dependencies first, inherit blocker state through parent-child hierarchy, execute children before closing parent/epic beads, then break ties by in-progress state, priority, type, and ID. Informational relationships like `related`, `relates-to`, `discovered-from`, and `supersedes` are not execution blockers.

The first execution run begins with the active/deploy-gating and highest-risk P1 beads:

`polylogue-s7ae.6` → classify the aborted full verify before coordination deploy.  
`polylogue-8jg9.4` → fix the ops-doctor blob-cleanup race.  
`polylogue-9e5.28` → make rigor audit iterate the product registry, not only declared contracts.  
`polylogue-9e5.29` → prevent numeric zero claims over absent evidence.  
`polylogue-9e5.30` → tag prose-mined forensic fields as text-derived.  
`polylogue-cpf.5` → propagate weakest temporal provenance through aggregates.  
`polylogue-cpf.6` → add a clock seam and audit `sort_key_ms` handling.  
`polylogue-kwsb.1` → harden daemon/capture Host, Origin, token, and spool controls.  
`polylogue-37t.15` → force non-user assertion writes through candidate/non-injected policy.  
`polylogue-83u.4` → classify missing referenced blobs in the production backup.  
`polylogue-cfk` → rerun the uplift experiment with fresh handoff packs.  
`polylogue-0v9p`, `polylogue-arso`, `polylogue-rlsb`, `polylogue-d4zk` → land the content-variant substrate and surfaces.  
`polylogue-d1y`, `polylogue-pj8`, `polylogue-s7ae.2`, `polylogue-ahqd`, `polylogue-37t.11`, `polylogue-s7ae.3`, `polylogue-s7ae.5` → install hooks, ship coordination MCP/cookbook surfaces, scheduler, coordination messages, adoption proof, and two-agent live proof.

After that, the plan proceeds through scale-hardening, lineage, query/read algebra, interactive performance, audit/provenance, web cockpit, analytics, interop/export, and frontier/vision features. The full artifact contains all 397 beads in exact order.

The precise end state after executing the whole schedule is this:

Polylogue has no remaining open/in-progress executable beads from this snapshot. All child beads are closed before their parent/epic closures, and no blocked Beads remain blocked in this tech-tree slice.

The archive substrate is scale-hardened. Blob cleanup cannot delete leased or in-flight blobs; production-backup blob debt is classified, restored where recoverable, or explicitly accepted; FTS/search/read-model drift is measured; large archive rebuilds and schema bumps use safe blue-green derived-tier replacement instead of long degraded windows.

Durable and derived storage tiers obey their intended regimes. `source.db` and `user.db` evolve through additive migrations with backup-manifest gates. `index.db` and `embeddings.db` rebuild or blue-green swap from durable evidence. `ops.db` remains disposable operational state.

Evidence honesty is enforced at the field level. Numeric fields distinguish absent evidence, true zero, and not applicable. Temporal aggregates propagate the weakest timestamp source. Prose-mined forensic facts carry text-derived caveats. The rigor audit covers every registered insight product or records an explicit exemption.

Agent coordination is operational. Hooks are installable and health-checked. MCP roles and prompts are discoverable. Agents can write benign, attributed records through the correct role. Candidate assertions go through one safe chokepoint. A context scheduler controls what enters agent context. A reproducible proof shows two agents in separate worktrees on one repo detecting overlap, exchanging a scoped message, receiving context injection, and producing a handoff packet.

Content variants are first-class archive objects. Language detection, preference facts, variant refs/nodes/alignment/storage, variant-aware projection/query/render profiles, and UX for creating/reviewing/messaging about variants all compose with the archive.

Session lineage is truthful and rebuild-stable. Shared content is stored once and counted once. Compaction boundaries, effective context, subagent/main-session distinctions, transcript completeness, physical identity collisions, compaction loss, and regrounding surfaces are represented explicitly.

The read surface is unified. CLI, daemon, MCP, Python API, web UI, and generated docs use the same Query × Projection × Render contract instead of parallel behavior. Surface-side math and duplicate dispatch paths are either deleted or routed through contracts.

Interactive performance is productized. CLI startup is light, common queries route through a hot daemon path, daemon caching/warming and push channels support live UIs, bulk ingest has bounded resource envelopes, and SLO/regression gates measure latency continuously.

The web workbench becomes an evidence cockpit. It supports evidence baskets, citable reports, verified exports, session replay, timeline/firehose views, daily narratives, live tailing, analytics views, long-session navigation, and citation anchors on top of the same evidence contracts.

Analytics answer “so what” questions without overclaiming. Work-graph units, outcome/pathology measures, temporal trends, process mining, survival analysis, prediction/calibration, experiment hosting, information-theoretic measures, trajectory-quality scoring, and model-drift observation are available with uncertainty and construct-validity limits.

Interop and export breadth expand. OriginSpec owns ingestion strictness and dispatch. Additional origins and trace formats become importable where scheduled. bash -lc python3 - <<'PY'
import json, collections
from pathlib import Path
base=Path('/mnt/data/polylogue_extract/polylogue')
export=base/'polylogue-beads-export.jsonl'
issues=[]; memories=[]; other=[]
for line in export.read_text().splitlines():
    o=json.loads(line)
    if o.get('_type')=='issue': issues.append(o)
    elif o.get('_type')=='memory': memories.append(o)
    else: other.append(o)
print('issues',len(issues),'mem',len(memories),'other',len(other))
keys=collections.Counter()
for i in issues: keys.update(i.keys())
print(keys)
print('sample issue')
for k,v in issues[0].items(): print(k, repr(v)[:400])
# count fields completeness on nonclosed
non=[i for i in issues if i.get('status')!='closed']
for field in ['description','acceptance_criteria','design','notes','labels','dependencies','assignee','created_at','updated_at','closed_at']:
    n=sum(1 for i in non if i.get(field) not in (None,'',[],{}))
    print(field,n,'/',len(non))
# analyze labels top
lab=collections.Counter(l for i in non for l in (i.get('labels') or []))
print('labels top', lab.most_common(50))

## 119. assistant

_create_time: 1783376325.399034_

bash -lc python3 - <<'PY'
import json, collections, re
from pathlib import Path
base=Path('/mnt/data/polylogue_extract/polylogue')
issues=[]
for line in (base/'polylogue-beads-export.jsonl').read_text().splitlines():
    o=json.loads(line)
    if o.get('_type')=='issue': issues.append(o)
ids={i['id']:i for i in issues}
non=[i for i in issues if i['status']!='closed']; nonids={i['id'] for i in non}
parent={}
children=collections.defaultdict(list)
blocks=collections.defaultdict(list)
for i in issues:
    for d in i.get('dependencies') or []:
        if d['type']=='parent-child': parent[i['id']]=d['depends_on_id']; children[d['depends_on_id']].append(i['id'])
        elif d['type']=='blocks': blocks[i['id']].append(d['depends_on_id'])

def root(iid):
    seen=set(); cur=iid
    while cur in parent and parent[cur] in ids and parent[cur] not in seen:
        seen.add(cur); cur=parent[cur]
    return cur
root_groups=collections.defaultdict(list)
for i in non:
    root_groups[root(i['id'])].append(i['id'])

def nk(s): return [int(p) if p.isdigit() else p for p in re.split('(\d+)',s)]
print('root count', len(root_groups))
for r,ms in sorted(root_groups.items(), key=lambda kv:(-len(kv[1]), ids[kv[0]].get('priority',9), nk(kv[0])))[:60]:
    ri=ids[r]
    print(f"{len(ms):3d} {r:16s} P{ri.get('priority')} {ri.get('issue_type'):7s} status {ri.get('status'):11s} title={ri.get('title')[:110]}")
# roots without open descendants? open root only once?
print('\nTop by priority')
for r,ms in sorted(root_groups.items(), key=lambda kv:(ids[kv[0]].get('priority',9), -len(kv[1]), nk(kv[0])))[:80]:
    ri=ids[r]
    print(f"{len(ms):3d} {r:16s} P{ri.get('priority')} {ri.get('issue_type'):7s} {ri.get('title')[:100]}")
PY

bash -lc python3 - <<'PY'
import json, collections
from pathlib import Path
base=Path('/mnt/data/polylogue_extract/polylogue')
issues=[]
for l in (base/'polylogue-beads-export.jsonl').read_text().splitlines():
 o=json.loads(l); 
 if o.get('_type')=='issue': issues.append(o)
ids={i['id']:i for i in issues}; nonids={i['id'] for i in issues if i.get('status')!='closed'}
counts=collections.Counter()
active_counts=collections.Counter()
missing=[]
for i in issues:
 for d in i.get('dependencies') or []:
  t=d.get('type'); dep=d.get('depends_on_id')
  counts[t]+=1
  if i['id'] in nonids and dep in nonids: active_counts[t]+=1
  if dep not in ids: missing.append((i['id'],t,dep))
print('dep type all',counts)
print('dep type active->active',active_counts)
print('missing deps',len(missing),missing[:10])
# containers no children?
children=collections.defaultdict(list)
for i in issues:
 for d in i.get('dependencies') or []:
  if d.get('type')=='parent-child': children[d.get('depends_on_id')].append(i['id'])
print('open epics no open children')
for i in issues:
 if i.get('issue_type')=='epic' and i['id'] in nonids:
  op=[c for c in children[i['id']] if c in nonids]
  if not op:
   print(i['id'],i['title'])
# orphan children with parent closed? or nonclosed child under closed root? open child with closed parent
print('open children with closed parent')
for i in issues:
 if i['id'] in nonids:
  for d in i.get('dependencies') or []:
   if d.get('type')=='parent-child' and ids.get(d.get('depends_on_id'),{}).get('status')=='closed':
    print(i['id'], 'parent closed', d.get('depends_on_id'), ids[d.get('depends_on_id')]['title'])

base=Path('/mnt/data/polylogue_extract/polylogue')

 o=json.loads(l)
 if o.get('_type')=='issue' and o.get('status')!='closed': active.append(o)
missing_ac=[i for i in active if not str(i.get('acceptance_criteria') or '').strip()]
print('missing_ac',len(missing_ac))
print('missing_ac notes present',sum(1 for i in missing_ac if str(i.get('notes') or '').strip()))
print('missing_ac design present',sum(1 for i in missing_ac if str(i.get('design') or '').strip()))
print('missing_ac desc present',sum(1 for i in missing_ac if str(i.get('description') or '').strip()))
for i in missing_ac[:5]:
 print(i['id'], 'notes?', bool(str(i.get('notes') or '').strip()), 'design?',bool(str(i.get('design') or '').strip()), i['title'])
# execution-grade if has description and (design or notes?) and (acceptance or notes?) maybe as per notes trap. Calculate variants.
def nonempty(i,f): return bool(str(i.get(f) or '').strip())
for name, pred in [
 ('strict desc+design+AC', lambda i: nonempty(i,'description') and nonempty(i,'design') and nonempty(i,'acceptance_criteria')),
 ('notes-as-AC desc+design+(AC or notes)', lambda i: nonempty(i,'description') and nonempty(i,'design') and (nonempty(i,'acceptance_criteria') or nonempty(i,'notes'))),
 ('notes-as-design-or-AC desc+(design or notes)+(AC or notes)', lambda i: nonempty(i,'description') and (nonempty(i,'design') or nonempty(i,'notes')) and (nonempty(i,'acceptance_criteria') or nonempty(i,'notes'))),
]:
 n=sum(1 for i in active if pred(i))
 print(name,n, f'{n/len(active)*100:.1f}%')

bash -lc python3 - <<'PY'
import json, collections
from pathlib import Path
base=Path('/mnt/data/polylogue_extract/polylogue')
active=[]
for l in (base/'polylogue-beads-export.jsonl').read_text().splitlines():
 o=json.loads(l)
 if o.get('_type')=='issue' and o.get('status')!='closed': active.append(o)
def ne(i,f): return bool(str(i.get(f) or '').strip())
def strict(i): return ne(i,'description') and ne(i,'design') and ne(i,'acceptance_criteria')
def note(i): return ne(i,'description') and (ne(i,'design') or ne(i,'notes')) and (ne(i,'acceptance_criteria') or ne(i,'notes'))
for p in [1,2,3,4]:
 items=[i for i in active if i['priority']==p]
 print('P',p,'n',len(items),'strict',sum(strict(i) for i in items), f'{sum(strict(i) for i in items)/len(items)*100:.1f}%', 'notes',sum(note(i) for i in items), f'{sum(note(i) for i in items)/len(items)*100:.1f}%')
for typ in ['bug','task','feature','epic','chore']:
 items=[i for i in active if i['issue_type']==typ]
 print(typ,'n',len(items),'strict',sum(strict(i) for i in items), f'{sum(strict(i) for i in items)/len(items)*100:.1f}%', 'notes',sum(note(i) for i in items), f'{sum(note(i) for i in items)/len(items)*100:.1f}%')

bash -lc python3 - <<'PY'
import json
from pathlib import Path
active=[]
for l in (Path('/mnt/data/polylogue_extract/polylogue')/'polylogue-beads-export.jsonl').read_text().splitlines():
 o=json.loads(l)
 if o.get('_type')=='issue' and o.get('status')!='closed': active.append(o)
def ne(i,f): return bool(str(i.get(f) or '').strip())
def strict(i): return ne(i,'description') and ne(i,'design') and ne(i,'acceptance_criteria')
def note(i): return ne(i,'description') and (ne(i,'design') or ne(i,'notes')) and (ne(i,'acceptance_criteria') or ne(i,'notes'))
items=[i for i in active if i['priority']<=2]
print(len(items), sum(strict(i) for i in items), sum(strict(i) for i in items)/len(items)*100, sum(note(i) for i in items), sum(note(i) for i in items)/len(items)*100)
# P1/P2 tasks/bugs only?
items=[i for i in active if i['priority']<=2 and i['issue_type'] in ('bug','task')]
print('P1P2 bug/task',len(items),sum(strict(i) for i in items),sum(strict(i) for i in items)/len(items)*100,sum(note(i) for i in items),sum(note(i) for i in items)/len(items)*100)

## 185. assistant

_create_time: 1783376969.984856_

Overall: the bead-set-implied plan is a strong architectural backlog and a credible dependency-aware execution map. It is not yet a fully implementation-ready delivery plan. Treat it as a complete inventory plus a safe topological ordering, not as a sprint schedule or release plan.

My scorecard:

| Dimension | Assessment |
| --- | --- |
| Backlog coverage | High. It includes all 397 non-closed executable issue beads from the snapshot. |
| Dependency hygiene | Good. I found no missing dependency references and no hard dependency cycles. |
| Architectural coherence | High. The work clusters around real product doctrines: evidence honesty, storage tier separation, provenance, query/render unification, agent coordination, lineage truth, interop, and external legibility. |
| Implementation readiness | Medium. P1/P2 safety and bug beads are mostly actionable; later P3/P4 feature beads are often roadmap/spec material. |
| Detail quality | Uneven but above average. Many beads have intent, design, and acceptance criteria; 72 active beads still lack acceptance criteria. |
| Scheduling quality | Weak-to-medium. Too many beads are “ready now,” so dependency ordering alone does not produce a useful delivery sequence. |
| End-state precision | Medium. The end state is coherent, but several clauses are product-vision statements rather than directly verifiable completion conditions. |

The biggest strength is that the bead set is not a generic wishlist. It is evidence-shaped. Many items point to real observed failures, named source files/modules, explicit verification expectations, and product invariants. For example, the first P1 items are not vague “improve reliability” work; they identify concrete hazards like unsafe blob cleanup, numeric claims over absent evidence, temporal provenance laundering, unsafe agent assertion promotion, missing production blobs, and an aborted full verification run. That is implementation-friendly.

The second major strength is thematic completeness. The plan covers the full system lifecycle: ingest, capture, storage, blobs, derived indexes, embeddings, assertions, preferences, query algebra, rendering, daemon, CLI, MCP, web UI, docs, demos, release proof, analytics, interop, and external publication. It also treats “truthfulness of evidence” as a cross-cutting product constraint rather than a documentation afterthought. That gives the plan a real spine.

The dependency graph itself is clean, but under-constraining. There are 623 exported dependency edges, including 125 `blocks` edges and 362 parent-child edges. After filtering to active work, the hard-blocker graph leaves 314 of 397 beads in wave 0. That means roughly 79% of the active backlog appears executable immediately. In practice, that is not true from an engineering-management perspective. It means the graph captures explicit blockers, but not enough architectural, migration, release, ownership, or sequencing constraints.

That is the most important flaw: the plan has false serial precision. A numbered order from 1 to 397 looks like “do this, then this, then this,” but most early ordering among unrelated wave-0 beads comes from priority/type/id tie-breaking, not real causality. The ordering is safe as a deterministic queue. It is not strong evidence that, say, every wave-0 web, query, analytics, content-variant, or interop task should actually be started before later blocked work unlocks.

The P1 layer is the most ready. All 32 P1 active beads have acceptance criteria. That part can be implemented almost directly, especially the stop-the-line work: classify the aborted verify, fix unsafe blob cleanup, harden daemon/capture security, prevent unsafe agent assertion activation, classify/restore missing blob debt, and repair rigor/provenance/numeric/temporal honesty gaps. This is the best-defined slice of the plan.

The P2 layer is mostly ready but needs local inspection before coding. There are 181 P2 beads; only 5 lack acceptance criteria. Many P2 items include enough design detail to start, but they span schema, derived models, UI, daemon paths, query contracts, release gates, and migration behavior. These should be batched into capability releases, not executed as isolated tickets.

The P3/P4 layer is substantially less ready. Among P3 beads, 60 of 166 lack acceptance criteria. Among P4 beads, 7 of 18 lack acceptance criteria. That is normal for horizon/backlog material, but it means the plan’s long tail is not implementation-ready. Those beads need design expansion, dependency normalization, test strategy, and milestone assignment before they become executable.

The bead detail is generally strong. Across the 397 active beads, 359 have descriptions, 363 have design text, and 325 have acceptance criteria. Around 80% mention verification/testing somewhere, and around 56% have explicit verify/test language in acceptance criteria. That is much better than a typical issue tracker. The detail weakness is not absence; it is inconsistency. Some beads are crisp enough to code; others are architectural slogans with partial execution shape.

There are some backlog-hygiene issues worth fixing before serious execution. The Beads summary has inconsistent readiness signals: the snapshot summary says 317 ready issues, while `ready_ids` contains 100, and blocked counts appear as 79 in one place and 83 after blocker propagation. That does not invalidate the plan, but it means readiness should be regenerated and linted before using it as an execution source of truth. Also, one open epic lacks acceptance criteria, and at least one open epic-like item has no open children, which suggests a few hierarchy/type cleanups are needed.

Completeness is strong at product-scope level and weaker at delivery-plan level. The bead set covers what the system should become, but it does not fully specify how the work is released. Missing delivery-layer information includes owners, estimates, batch size, branch/PR boundaries, migration order, rollback strategy, compatibility matrix, demo/proof cut lines, release gates, and “do not start before X stabilizes” soft dependencies. Those are not usually stored in a bead title/description, but they are necessary for execution.

The plan also does not fully integrate the 22 Beads memory records into the execution order. Some memories encode process invariants, such as bead field-update discipline, automatic convergence expectations, and backlog linting. Those are not executable beads, but they should affect implementation. Ignoring them risks violating project-specific operating rules while still “following the plan.”

The end state is directionally correct but not precise enough as a verification target. Statements like “Polylogue is the local system of record for AI work” and “the web workbench becomes an evidence cockpit” describe the intended product, but they are not directly testable. A precise end state needs a claims ledger mapping each final-state sentence to bead IDs, schema versions, commands, fixtures, proof artifacts, and required passing validation lanes.

The highest-risk areas are schema/migration coupling, derived-tier rebuild correctness, data-loss paths, security boundaries, surface-contract drift, and performance regressions. The plan notices most of these risks, which is good. But because many related items are not hard-linked, an implementer could accidentally build UI or analytics on top of unstable contracts, then pay integration debt later.

The best way to execute this plan is not bead #1 through bead #397. The right execution shape is phased:

First, close operational safety and evidence-honesty gates: verify classification, blob safety, daemon security, assertion safety, missing blob debt, temporal/numeric/provenance rigor, and backup/degraded-state correctness.

Second, stabilize substrate contracts: storage tier separation, migration/rebuild invariants, source/origin specs, query/projection/render contracts, assertion/candidate policy, and schema ownership.

Third, build product surfaces on those contracts: coordination substrate, content variants, lineage truth, MCP/CLI/API convergence, webui v2, evidence baskets, live tailing, reports, and export lanes.

Fourth, expand analytics and interop: work-graph units, outcome measures, process mining, prediction/calibration, external trace formats, federation, PKM/export, and research-tooling formats.

Fifth, close external legibility: README, one-command demo, public claims ledger, install matrix, proof cards, docs site, launch kit, and published findings.

So the verdict is: high-quality backlog, strong architectural plan, medium implementation readiness, and uneven detail. It is ready for immediate execution on P1/P2 safety and correctness work. It is not ready to execute blindly as a 397-step linear plan. Before broad implementation, it needs a short normalization pass: reconcile readiness counts, run bead lint fresh, add missing acceptance criteria for P2+ work, convert hidden architectural dependencies into explicit `blocks` edges, split large horizon features, and define release gates.

import json, collections, textwrap
p='/mnt/data/polylogue_extract/polylogue/polylogue-beads-export.jsonl'
issues=[]
mem=[]
for line in open(p):
    obj=json.loads(line)
    if obj.get('_type')=='issue': issues.append(obj)
    elif obj.get('_type')=='memory': mem.append(obj)
    else: print('other',obj.get('_type'))
print('issues',len(issues),'mem',len(mem))
for field in ['status','priority','issue_type','type']:
    c=collections.Counter(i.get(field) for i in issues)
    print(field,c)
# sample keys
print(issues[0].keys())
print(mem[:1])
# ids by status
for st,c in collections.Counter(i.get('status') for i in issues).items(): print(st,c)
# count open nonclosed
active=[i for i in issues if i.get('status')!='closed']
print('active',len(active))
print(collections.Counter(i.get('status') for i in active))
print(collections.Counter(i.get('priority') for i in active))
print(collections.Counter(i.get('issue_type') for i in active))
# output top titles by priority active
for pr in ['P0','P1','P2','P3','P4',None]:
    arr=[i for i in active if i.get('priority')==pr]
    if arr:
      print('\n',pr,len(arr))
      for i in arr[:20]: print(i['id'], i.get('issue_type'), i.get('status'), i['title'][:100])

bash -lc python - <<'PY'
import json, collections, textwrap
issues=[json.loads(l) for l in open('/mnt/data/polylogue_extract/polylogue/polylogue-beads-export.jsonl') if json.loads(l).get('_type')=='issue']
ids={i['id']:i for i in issues}
children=collections.defaultdict(list)
for i in issues:
 for d in i.get('dependencies') or []:
  if d.get('type')=='parent-child': children[d['depends_on_id']].append(i['id'])
for id,i in sorted(ids.items(), key=lambda kv:(kv[1].get('priority',9), kv[1]['id'])):
 if i.get('issue_type')=='epic' or id in children:
  arr=children.get(id,[])
  active=sum(ids[c].get('status')!='closed' for c in arr)
  closed=sum(ids[c].get('status')=='closed' for c in arr)
  print(f"{id} P{i.get('priority')} {i.get('status')} {i.get('issue_type')} children={len(arr)} active={active} closed={closed} | {i['title']}")
  # print child titles short maybe for active epics up to 12
  if i.get('status')!='closed':
   for c in sorted(arr, key=lambda x:(ids[x].get('priority',9), x))[:15]:
    ci=ids[c]
    print(f"   - {c} P{ci.get('priority')} {ci.get('status')} {ci.get('issue_type')}: {ci['title'][:95]}")

import json, collections
issues=[]
with open('/mnt/data/polylogue_extract/polylogue/polylogue-beads-export.jsonl') as f:
 for line in f:
  obj=json.loads(line)
  if obj.get('_type')=='issue': issues.append(obj)
ids={i['id']:i for i in issues}
children=collections.defaultdict(list)
for i in issues:
 for d in i.get('dependencies') or []:
  if d.get('type')=='parent-child': children[d['depends_on_id']].append(i['id'])
for id,i in sorted(ids.items(), key=lambda kv:(kv[1].get('priority',9), kv[1]['id'])):
 if i.get('issue_type')=='epic' or id in children:
  arr=children.get(id,[])
  active=sum(ids[c].get('status')!='closed' for c in arr)
  closed=sum(ids[c].get('status')=='closed' for c in arr)
  print(f"{id} P{i.get('priority')} {i.get('status')} {i.get('issue_type')} children={len(arr)} active={active} closed={closed} | {i['title']}")
  if i.get('status')!='closed':
   for c in sorted(arr, key=lambda x:(ids[x].get('priority',9), x)):
    ci=ids[c]
    print(f"   - {c} P{ci.get('priority')} {ci.get('status')} {ci.get('issue_type')}: {ci['title']}")
print('DONE')

bash -lc python - <<'PY'
import json, collections, re, statistics
issues=[]; memories=[]
for l in open('/mnt/data/polylogue_extract/polylogue/polylogue-beads-export.jsonl'):
 obj=json.loads(l)
 if obj.get('_type')=='issue': issues.append(obj)
 elif obj.get('_type')=='memory': memories.append(obj)
active=[i for i in issues if i.get('status')!='closed']
closed=[i for i in issues if i.get('status')=='closed']
def has(field,i): return bool(str(i.get(field) or '').strip())
print('all',len(issues),'active',len(active),'closed',len(closed),'mem',len(memories))
print('active by priority/type')
for pr in sorted(set(i.get('priority') for i in active)):
 print('P'+str(pr),len([i for i in active if i.get('priority')==pr]), collections.Counter(i.get('issue_type') for i in active if i.get('priority')==pr))
print('\nmissing fields active by priority')
for pr in sorted(set(i.get('priority') for i in active)):
 arr=[i for i in active if i.get('priority')==pr]
 print('P'+str(pr),'n',len(arr),'no desc',sum(not has('description',i) for i in arr),'no design',sum(not has('design',i) for i in arr),'no ac',sum(not has('acceptance_criteria',i) for i in arr),'notes',sum(has('notes',i) for i in arr))
print('\nall field coverage')
for group,arr in [('active',active),('closed',closed),('all',issues)]:
 print(group, 'desc',sum(has('description',i) for i in arr),'design',sum(has('design',i) for i in arr),'ac',sum(has('acceptance_criteria',i) for i in arr),'notes',sum(has('notes',i) for i in arr),'closed_reason',sum(has('close_reason',i) for i in arr))
print('\nhorizon counts')
for group,arr in [('active',active),('closed',closed)]:
 c=collections.Counter()
 for i in arr:
  labs=i.get('labels') or []
  h=[l for l in labs if l.startswith('horizon:')]
  if not h: c['no horizon']+=1
  else:
   for l in h:c[l]+=1
 print(group,c)
print('\nactive labels area top')
labs=collections.Counter()
for i in active:
 for l in i.get('labels') or []:
  if l.startswith('area:'): labs[l]+=1
for k,v in labs.most_common(): print(k,v)
print('\nclosed priority type')
for pr in sorted(set(i.get('priority') for i in closed)):
 print('P'+str(pr), len([i for i in closed if i.get('priority')==pr]), collections.Counter(i.get('issue_type') for i in closed if i.get('priority')==pr))
# Dependencies active hard
print('\ndep counts')
C=collections.Counter()
C_active=collections.Counter()
for i in issues:
 for d in i.get('dependencies') or []:
  C[d['type']]+=1
  if i in active: C_active[d['type']]+=1
print('all',C); print('active issue side',C_active)
