    ('P11','Variants substrate','polylogue-0v9p',['polylogue-0v9p','polylogue-arso','polylogue-rlsb','polylogue-d4zk'],'E-VARIANTS-PREFERENCES','Mixed-language fixture with original text, transformed variants, alignment, and review state.'),
    ('P12','Blue-green rebuild','polylogue-b5l',['polylogue-20d.15','polylogue-b5l','polylogue-1xc.8'],'B-STORAGE-REBUILD-BYTES','No partial-ready state; old generation serves while new generation builds and swaps safely.'),
    ('P13','Lineage and compaction recovery','polylogue-4ts.5',['polylogue-4ts.5','polylogue-gjg.1','polylogue-gjg.2','polylogue-gjg.3','polylogue-gjg.4'],'F-LINEAGE-COMPACTION','Compaction boundaries, pre-compaction snapshots, loss forensics, and scheduler-mediated regrounding proof.'),
    ('P14','Live capture and push path','polylogue-20d.13',['polylogue-20d.1','polylogue-20d.12','polylogue-20d.13','polylogue-3v1.1'],'G-LIVE-PERFORMANCE-CAPTURE','Daemon fast path, cache invalidation, push events, and concurrent capture fixture.'),
    ('P15','Web evidence basket','polylogue-bby.15',['polylogue-bby.11','polylogue-bby.15','polylogue-bby.8'],'H-WEB-EVIDENCE-COCKPIT','Evidence basket, citable report, verified export, and visual smoke artifact.'),
    ('P16','Stats registry and experiments','polylogue-9l5.7',['polylogue-9l5.7','polylogue-stc','polylogue-cfk'],'I-ANALYTICS-EXPERIMENTS','Registered measures with uncertainty/sample-frame metadata and refreshed uplift experiment artifact.'),
    ('P17','Semantic retrieval lane','polylogue-mhx.1',['polylogue-mhx.1','polylogue-mhx.2','polylogue-mhx.3','polylogue-mhx.4'],'J-EMBEDDINGS-SEMANTIC','Provider abstraction, target policy, retrieval quality eval, and scheduler-safe context leg.'),
    ('P18','OriginSpec and export idempotence','polylogue-2qx',['polylogue-2qx','polylogue-l4kf.1','polylogue-uiw'],'K-INTEROP-ORIGINS-EXPORT','Declared origin contracts and content-hash idempotent Polylogue export/import envelope.'),
    ('P19','Public proof and launch kit','polylogue-3tl.16',['polylogue-3tl.16','polylogue-3tl.4','polylogue-3tl.7','polylogue-3tl.10'],'L-EXTERNAL-LEGIBILITY-LAUNCH','Claims ledger, published finding, install matrix, README/launch kit, and cold-reader pass.'),
    ('P20','Substrate consolidation after contracts','polylogue-hiu',['polylogue-pf1','polylogue-exb','polylogue-hiu','polylogue-4822'],'M-SUBSTRATE-CONSOLIDATION','Before/after parity report, layering check, storage twin collapse, public model boundary.'),
]
packet_rows = []
for seq, name, primary, beads, release, proof in PACKETS:
    packet_rows.append({
        'packet_id': seq,
        'name': name,
        'primary_bead': primary,
        'included_beads': ', '.join([b for b in beads if b in issues]),
        'release_key': release,
        'lane': release_by_key[release]['lane'],
        'entry_gate': release_by_key[release]['entry_gate'],
        'proof_artifact': proof,
        'verify': release_by_key[release]['verification'],
        'rollback': release_by_key[release]['rollback'],
    })

# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Write files
# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
def write_jsonl(path: Path, rows):
    with path.open('w', encoding='utf-8') as f:
        for row in rows:
            f.write(json.dumps(row, ensure_ascii=False, sort_keys=True) + '\n')

def write_csv(path: Path, rows):
    if not rows:
        path.write_text('')
        return
    fieldnames = list(rows[0].keys())
    with path.open('w', newline='', encoding='utf-8') as f:
        w = csv.DictWriter(f, fieldnames=fieldnames)
        w.writeheader()
        w.writerows(rows)

write_jsonl(OUT / 'delivery_manifest.jsonl', manifest_rows)
write_csv(OUT / 'delivery_manifest.csv', manifest_rows)
write_jsonl(OUT / 'acceptance_criteria_patches.jsonl', acceptance_patches)
write_csv(OUT / 'acceptance_criteria_patches.csv', acceptance_patches)
write_jsonl(OUT / 'dependency_additions.jsonl', proposed_edges)
write_csv(OUT / 'dependency_additions.csv', proposed_edges)
write_jsonl(OUT / 'label_patches.jsonl', label_patches)
write_jsonl(OUT / 'beads_upgrade_patch.jsonl', combined_patch)
write_jsonl(OUT / 'implementation_packets.jsonl', packet_rows)
write_csv(OUT / 'implementation_packets.csv', packet_rows)
write_jsonl(OUT / 'release_gates.jsonl', RELEASES)
write_csv(OUT / 'release_gates.csv', RELEASES)
write_jsonl(OUT / 'polylogue-beads-upgraded-candidate.jsonl', upgraded_objects)

# Release gates YAML (simple hand-rolled)
yaml_lines = ['# Polylogue Beads delivery release gates', 'generated_at: "' + datetime.now(timezone.utc).replace(microsecond=0).isoformat().replace('+00:00','Z') + '"', 'releases:']
for r in RELEASES:
    yaml_lines.append(f"  - key: {r['key']}")
    yaml_lines.append(f"    number: {r['number']}")
    yaml_lines.append(f"    name: {json.dumps(r['name'])}")
    yaml_lines.append(f"    lane: {r['lane']}")
    for k in ['purpose','entry_gate','exit_gate','verification','rollback']:
        yaml_lines.append(f"    {k}: {json.dumps(r[k])}")
(OUT / 'release_gates.yaml').write_text('\n'.join(yaml_lines) + '\n', encoding='utf-8')

# Markdown summaries
summary_counts = Counter(r['release_key'] for r in manifest_rows)
readiness_counts = Counter(r['readiness_grade'] for r in manifest_rows)
queue_counts = Counter(r['implementation_queue'] for r in manifest_rows)
priority_counts = Counter(str(r['priority']) for r in manifest_rows)

readme = f"""# Polylogue Beads upgrade bundle

Generated from the uploaded `polylogue-beads-export.jsonl` and the execution-order CSV on {datetime.now(timezone.utc).replace(microsecond=0).isoformat().replace('+00:00','Z')}.

This bundle turns the dependency-aware bead inventory into a reviewable implementation setup. It does **not** require blindly overwriting the tracker. The safest path is to review the patch files, then apply the parts you accept through Beads tooling.

## What changed conceptually

The old execution order is preserved as `order` in `delivery_manifest.*`, but the backlog is now organized as releases with entry gates, exit gates, proof artifacts, rollback/degraded-mode notes, readiness grades, and proposed hidden blockers.

Readiness grades:

- **A** — implement now: acceptance criteria plus enough description/design to start safely.
- **B** — inspect then implement: acceptance criteria exist, but description or design needs local confirmation.
- **C** — spec first: active P1/P2 bead lacked acceptance criteria; a proposed patch is included.
- **D** — future-ready: later-horizon bead has execution shape but should wait for gates.
- **E** — parked/spec: do not code directly yet.

## Inventory

- Active beads in manifest: **{len(manifest_rows)}**
- Release count: **{len(RELEASES)}**
- Proposed dependency additions: **{len(proposed_edges)}**
- Missing acceptance criteria patched: **{len(acceptance_patches)}**
- Label patch operations: **{len(label_patches)}**
- Implementation packets: **{len(packet_rows)}**

Readiness counts: {', '.join(f'{k}: {v}' for k, v in sorted(readiness_counts.items()))}.

Queue counts: {', '.join(f'{k}: {v}' for k, v in sorted(queue_counts.items()))}.

## Files

| File | Purpose |
| --- | --- |
| `delivery_manifest.csv` / `.jsonl` | One row per active bead with release, lane, readiness, proof, rollback, risks, and acceptance text. |
| `release_gates.yaml` / `.csv` / `.jsonl` | Gate definitions for the phased delivery plan. |
| `implementation_packets.csv` / `.jsonl` | PR-shaped packets that turn large release gates into concrete implementation chunks. |
| `dependency_additions.csv` / `.jsonl` | Proposed hidden blockers to promote into `blocks` relationships after review. |
| `acceptance_criteria_patches.csv` / `.jsonl` | Proposed acceptance criteria for every active bead that was missing AC. |
| `label_patches.jsonl` | Suggested delivery/readiness/queue labels for active beads. |
| `beads_upgrade_patch.jsonl` | Combined patch stream: labels, AC, and dependency additions. |
| `polylogue-beads-upgraded-candidate.jsonl` | Candidate full Beads export with labels, missing AC filled, and proposed blocker edges embedded. Review before import. |
| `UPGRADE_PLAN.md` | Human-readable upgraded delivery plan. |
| `APPLYING.md` | Safe application instructions. |

## Important safety note

`polylogue-beads-upgraded-candidate.jsonl` is a candidate export, not an instruction to overwrite your live Beads state without review. The safer workflow is:

1. Inspect `acceptance_criteria_patches.*` and apply the 5 P2 patches first.
2. Inspect `dependency_additions.*`; promote only accepted soft blockers into Beads.
3. Add labels from `label_patches.jsonl` if you want delivery queues visible in Beads.
4. Regenerate `bd ready --json` / bead lint and compare against this manifest.

"""
(OUT / 'README.md').write_text(readme, encoding='utf-8')

# Human plan markdown
plan_lines = [
    '# Upgraded Beads delivery plan',
    '',
    'This is the gated implementation setup derived from the full active bead set. The original topological order remains a safe queue, but the actual implementation plan is release-gated and proof-driven.',
    '',
    '## Release spine',
    '',
]
for r in RELEASES:
    plan_lines.extend([
        f"### {r['number']}. {r['key']} — {r['name']}",
        '',
        f"**Lane:** {r['lane']}",
        '',
        f"**Purpose:** {r['purpose']}",
        '',
        f"**Entry gate:** {r['entry_gate']}",
        '',
        f"**Exit gate:** {r['exit_gate']}",
        '',
        f"**Verification:** {r['verification']}",
        '',
        f"**Rollback/degrade:** {r['rollback']}",
        '',
        f"**Active beads assigned:** {summary_counts.get(r['key'],0)}",
        '',
    ])
plan_lines.extend(['## Implementation packets', ''])
for p in packet_rows:
    plan_lines.extend([
        f"### {p['packet_id']} — {p['name']}",
        '',
        f"Primary bead: `{p['primary_bead']}`",
        '',
        f"Included beads: `{p['included_beads']}`",
        '',
        f"Release: `{p['release_key']}` / lane `{p['lane']}`",
        '',
        f"Proof artifact: {p['proof_artifact']}",
        '',
    ])
plan_lines.extend(['## Readiness summary', ''])
for grade in ['A','B','C','D','E']:
    plan_lines.append(f"- **{grade}:** {readiness_counts.get(grade,0)} — {readiness_meaning(grade)}")
plan_lines.extend(['', '## Release counts', ''])
plan_lines.append('| Release | Beads |')
plan_lines.append('| --- | ---: |')
for r in RELEASES:
    plan_lines.append(f"| {r['key']} | {summary_counts.get(r['key'],0)} |")
plan_lines.extend(['', '## The upgraded execution rule', '', 'Do not run the 397 beads as a blind line. Run the earliest implementable packet whose release entry gate is satisfied. Close child beads before parent epics. Publish no claim without evidence refs. Let no agent-authored assertion become injected memory without judgment. Treat storage, byte integrity, provenance, and daemon security as release gates, not optional hardening.'])
(OUT / 'UPGRADE_PLAN.md').write_text('\n'.join(plan_lines) + '\n', encoding='utf-8')

apply_md = """# Applying this upgrade safely

This bundle is designed for review-first application.

## Recommended application order

1. Open `delivery_manifest.csv` and filter `priority <= 2` plus `readiness_grade = C`. Apply the five P2 acceptance-criteria patches first.
2. Review `dependency_additions.csv`. Add the blocker edges that reflect real architecture, not just planning preference.
3. Apply `label_patches.jsonl` if you want delivery queues visible in Beads.
4. Regenerate Beads readiness/lint.
5. Compare Beads-ready work against `implementation_packets.csv`.

## Patch semantics

`acceptance_criteria_patches.jsonl` rows mean: replace empty acceptance criteria only.

`dependency_additions.jsonl` rows mean: add a hard `blocks` edge if, after review, the reason is accepted.

`label_patches.jsonl` rows mean: add classification labels only; they do not change task semantics.

`polylogue-beads-upgraded-candidate.jsonl` is a full candidate export created by applying all patches to the exported JSONL snapshot. Use it for diff/review or as an import source only if your Beads workflow supports full-export replacement safely.

## Suggested review commands

```bash
# In the Polylogue repo, after copying this bundle into the worktree:
python -m json.tool < beads_upgrade_patch.jsonl >/dev/null
python -m json.tool < release_gates.jsonl >/dev/null

# Review priority-2 spec gaps first:
python - <<'PY'
import json
for line in open('acceptance_criteria_patches.jsonl'):
    row=json.loads(line)
    if row['priority'] <= 2:
        print(row['issue_id'], row['title'])
        print(row['acceptance_criteria'])
        print()
PY
```

Exact Beads CLI mutation commands are intentionally not baked in here because this archive did not include a local `bd` binary or command reference for dependency mutation syntax. The machine-readable patch stream is the source of truth.
"""
(OUT / 'APPLYING.md').write_text(apply_md, encoding='utf-8')

# Markdown tables for patches/deps
ac_md = ['# Acceptance criteria patches', '', '| Priority | Bead | Release | Title | Proposed acceptance criteria |', '| ---: | --- | --- | --- | --- |']
for r in acceptance_patches:
    ac_md.append('| {priority} | `{issue_id}` | `{release_key}` | {title} | {ac} |'.format(
        priority=r['priority'], issue_id=r['issue_id'], release_key=r['release_key'], title=r['title'].replace('|','\\|'), ac=r['acceptance_criteria'].replace('|','\\|')
    ))
(OUT / 'ACCEPTANCE_CRITERIA_PATCHES.md').write_text('\n'.join(ac_md)+'\n', encoding='utf-8')

dep_md = ['# Proposed dependency additions', '', '| Issue | Blocks on | Reason |', '| --- | --- | --- |']
for e in proposed_edges:
    dep_md.append(f"| `{e['issue_id']}` | `{e['depends_on_id']}` | {e['reason'].replace('|','\\|')} |")
(OUT / 'DEPENDENCY_ADDITIONS.md').write_text('\n'.join(dep_md)+'\n', encoding='utf-8')

# Delivery manifest compact markdown, grouped by release
manifest_md = ['# Delivery manifest — compact', '']
for r in RELEASES:
    rows = [m for m in manifest_rows if m['release_key'] == r['key']]
    if not rows:
        continue
    manifest_md.append(f"## {r['key']} — {r['name']} ({len(rows)} beads)")
    manifest_md.append('')
    manifest_md.append('| Order | Grade | Queue | Bead | P | Type | Title | Proposed blockers |')
    manifest_md.append('| ---: | --- | --- | --- | ---: | --- | --- | --- |')
    for m in rows:
        blockers = m['proposed_soft_blockers_to_promote'] or ''
        manifest_md.append(f"| {m['order']} | {m['readiness_grade']} | {m['implementation_queue']} | `{m['id']}` | {m['priority']} | {m['type']} | {m['title'].replace('|','\\|')} | {blockers} |")
    manifest_md.append('')
(OUT / 'DELIVERY_MANIFEST_COMPACT.md').write_text('\n'.join(manifest_md)+'\n', encoding='utf-8')

# Machine-readable summary
summary = {
    'generated_at': datetime.now(timezone.utc).replace(microsecond=0).isoformat().replace('+00:00','Z'),
    'input_beads_export': str(BEADS),
    'input_order_csv': str(ORDER_CSV),
    'active_beads': len(manifest_rows),
    'release_count': len(RELEASES),
    'release_counts': dict(summary_counts),
    'readiness_counts': dict(readiness_counts),
    'queue_counts': dict(queue_counts),
    'priority_counts': dict(priority_counts),
    'acceptance_patches': len(acceptance_patches),
    'dependency_additions': len(proposed_edges),
    'label_patches': len(label_patches),
    'implementation_packets': len(packet_rows),
}
(OUT / 'upgrade_summary.json').write_text(json.dumps(summary, indent=2, sort_keys=True), encoding='utf-8')

# Validate no dangling patch dependencies
missing = []
for e in proposed_edges:
    if e['issue_id'] not in issues or e['depends_on_id'] not in issues:
        missing.append(e)
assert not missing, missing[:3]
assert len(manifest_rows) == len(active_ids)

# Build tarball and zip
archive_base = ROOT / 'polylogue_beads_upgrade_bundle'
# Remove stale tar/zip if any
for ext in ['.tar.gz', '.zip']:
    p = ROOT / f'polylogue_beads_upgrade_bundle{ext}'
    if p.exists():
        p.unlink()
with tarfile.open(ROOT / 'polylogue_beads_upgrade_bundle.tar.gz', 'w:gz') as tar:
    tar.add(OUT, arcname='polylogue_beads_upgrade_bundle')
shutil.make_archive(str(ROOT / 'polylogue_beads_upgrade_bundle'), 'zip', OUT)
print(json.dumps(summary, indent=2, sort_keys=True))
print('OUT', OUT)

# Markdown tables for patches/deps

        priority=r['priority'], issue_id=r['issue_id'], release_key=r['release_key'], title=r['title'].replace('|','\\|'), ac=r['acceptance_criteria'].replace('|','\\|')
    ))

for e in proposed_edges:
    dep_md.append('| `{}` | `{}` | {} |'.format(e['issue_id'], e['depends_on_id'], e['reason'].replace('|','\\|')))
(OUT / 'DEPENDENCY_ADDITIONS.md').write_text('\n'.join(dep_md)+'\n', encoding='utf-8')

# Delivery manifest compact markdown, grouped by release
manifest_md = ['# Delivery manifest — compact', '']
for r in RELEASES:
    rows = [m for m in manifest_rows if m['release_key'] == r['key']]
    if not rows:
        continue
    manifest_md.append(f"## {r['key']} — {r['name']} ({len(rows)} beads)")
    manifest_md.append('')
    manifest_md.append('| Order | Grade | Queue | Bead | P | Type | Title | Proposed blockers |')
    manifest_md.append('| ---: | --- | --- | --- | ---: | --- | --- | --- |')
    for m in rows:
        blockers = m['proposed_soft_blockers_to_promote'] or ''
        safe_title = m['title'].replace('|','\\|')
        manifest_md.append(f"| {m['order']} | {m['readiness_grade']} | {m['implementation_queue']} | `{m['id']}` | {m['priority']} | {m['type']} | {safe_title} | {blockers} |")
    manifest_md.append('')
(OUT / 'DELIVERY_MANIFEST_COMPACT.md').write_text('\n'.join(manifest_md)+'\n', encoding='utf-8')

# Machine-readable summary
summary = {
    'generated_at': datetime.now(timezone.utc).replace(microsecond=0).isoformat().replace('+00:00','Z'),
    'input_beads_export': str(BEADS),
    'input_order_csv': str(ORDER_CSV),
    'active_beads': len(manifest_rows),
    'release_count': len(RELEASES),
    'release_counts': dict(summary_counts),
    'readiness_counts': dict(readiness_counts),
    'queue_counts': dict(queue_counts),
    'priority_counts': dict(priority_counts),
    'acceptance_patches': len(acceptance_patches),
    'dependency_additions': len(proposed_edges),
    'label_patches': len(label_patches),
    'implementation_packets': len(packet_rows),
}
(OUT / 'upgrade_summary.json').write_text(json.dumps(summary, indent=2, sort_keys=True), encoding='utf-8')

# Validate no dangling patch dependencies
missing = []
for e in proposed_edges:
    if e['issue_id'] not in issues or e['depends_on_id'] not in issues:
        missing.append(e)
assert not missing, missing[:3]
assert len(manifest_rows) == len(active_ids)

# Build tarball and zip
for ext in ['.tar.gz', '.zip']:
    p = ROOT / f'polylogue_beads_upgrade_bundle{ext}'
    if p.exists():
        p.unlink()
with tarfile.open(ROOT / 'polylogue_beads_upgrade_bundle.tar.gz', 'w:gz') as tar:
    tar.add(OUT, arcname='polylogue_beads_upgrade_bundle')
shutil.make_archive(str(ROOT / 'polylogue_beads_upgrade_bundle'), 'zip', OUT)
print(json.dumps(summary, indent=2, sort_keys=True))
print('OUT', OUT)
__TAIL_EOF__

bash -lc cat > /mnt/data/create_beads_upgrade_workbook.py <<'PY'
from __future__ import annotations

import csv
import json
from pathlib import Path
from artifact_tool import Workbook, SpreadsheetFile

ROOT = Path('/mnt/data')
B = ROOT / 'polylogue_beads_upgrade_bundle'
OUT = ROOT / 'polylogue_beads_upgrade_dashboard.xlsx'


def read_csv(name):
    with (B / name).open(newline='', encoding='utf-8') as f:
        return list(csv.DictReader(f))

manifest = read_csv('delivery_manifest.csv')
releases = read_csv('release_gates.csv')
deps = read_csv('dependency_additions.csv')
ac = read_csv('acceptance_criteria_patches.csv')
packets = read_csv('implementation_packets.csv')
summary = json.loads((B / 'upgrade_summary.json').read_text())

wb = Workbook.create()

header_fmt = {
    'fill': '#0F766E',
    'font': {'bold': True, 'color': '#FFFFFF'},
    'horizontal_alignment': 'center',
    'vertical_alignment': 'center',
    'wrap_text': True,
}
subheader_fmt = {
    'fill': '#CCFBF1',
    'font': {'bold': True, 'color': '#0F172A'},
    'horizontal_alignment': 'center',
    'vertical_alignment': 'center',
    'wrap_text': True,
}
text_fmt = {'wrap_text': True, 'vertical_alignment': 'top'}

# Dashboard
sh = wb.worksheets.add('Dashboard')
sh.get_range('A1:H1').merge()
sh.get_range('A1').values = [['Polylogue Beads Upgrade Dashboard']]
sh.get_range('A1').format = {'fill': '#0F766E', 'font': {'bold': True, 'color': '#FFFFFF', 'size': 16}, 'horizontal_alignment': 'center'}
sh.get_range('A3:B10').values = [
    ['Metric', 'Value'],
    ['Active beads', summary['active_beads']],
    ['Release gates', summary['release_count']],
    ['Proposed dependency additions', summary['dependency_additions']],
    ['Acceptance criteria patches', summary['acceptance_patches']],
    ['Label patch operations', summary['label_patches']],
    ['Implementation packets', summary['implementation_packets']],
    ['Generated at', summary['generated_at']],
]
sh.get_range('A3:B3').format = header_fmt
sh.get_range('A4:B10').format = text_fmt
sh.get_range('D3:F3').values = [['Readiness', 'Count', 'Meaning']]
sh.get_range('D3:F3').format = header_fmt
readiness_meanings = {
    'A': 'Implement now', 'B': 'Inspect then implement', 'C': 'Spec first', 'D': 'Future-ready', 'E': 'Park/spec'
}
readiness_rows = []
for grade in ['A','B','C','D','E']:
    readiness_rows.append([grade, summary['readiness_counts'].get(grade, 0), readiness_meanings[grade]])
sh.get_range(f'D4:F{3+len(readiness_rows)}').values = readiness_rows
sh.get_range('D4:F8').format = text_fmt

sh.get_range('A13:D13').values = [['Release', 'Lane', 'Beads', 'Exit gate']]
sh.get_range('A13:D13').format = header_fmt
rel_rows = []
for r in releases:
    rel_rows.append([r['key'], r['lane'], summary['release_counts'].get(r['key'], 0), r['exit_gate']])
sh.get_range(f'A14:D{13+len(rel_rows)}').values = rel_rows
sh.get_range(f'A14:D{13+len(rel_rows)}').format = text_fmt
sh.get_range('A:A').format.column_width = 28
sh.get_range('B:B').format.column_width = 22
sh.get_range('C:C').format.column_width = 12
sh.get_range('D:D').format.column_width = 70
sh.get_range('F:F').format.column_width = 28
sh.freeze_panes.freeze_rows(3)
try:
    sh.tables.add(f'A13:D{13+len(rel_rows)}', True, 'DashboardReleaseTable')
except Exception:
    pass

# Release gates
rg = wb.worksheets.add('Release_Gates')
rg_cols = ['number','key','lane','name','purpose','entry_gate','exit_gate','verification','rollback']
rg_data = [rg_cols] + [[r.get(c,'') for c in rg_cols] for r in releases]
rg.get_range_by_indexes(0, 0, len(rg_data), len(rg_cols)).values = rg_data
rg.get_range_by_indexes(0,0,1,len(rg_cols)).format = header_fmt
rg.get_range_by_indexes(1,0,len(rg_data)-1,len(rg_cols)).format = text_fmt
rg.freeze_panes.freeze_rows(1)
rg.get_range('A:A').format.column_width = 8
rg.get_range('B:B').format.column_width = 28
rg.get_range('C:C').format.column_width = 20
rg.get_range('D:D').format.column_width = 34
rg.get_range('E:I').format.column_width = 48
try:
    rg.tables.add(f'A1:I{len(rg_data)}', True, 'ReleaseGatesTable')
except Exception:
    pass

# Manifest (compact columns)
mf = wb.worksheets.add('Manifest')
mf_cols = ['order','id','title','priority','type','status','release_key','lane','readiness_grade','implementation_queue','proposed_soft_blockers_to_promote','proof_expectation','public_claim_impact','security_privacy_impact','data_loss_impact','migration_impact']
mf_data = [mf_cols] + [[m.get(c,'') for c in mf_cols] for m in manifest]
mf.get_range_by_indexes(0,0,len(mf_data),len(mf_cols)).values = mf_data
mf.get_range_by_indexes(0,0,1,len(mf_cols)).format = header_fmt
mf.get_range_by_indexes(1,0,len(mf_data)-1,len(mf_cols)).format = text_fmt
mf.freeze_panes.freeze_rows(1)
mf.freeze_panes.freeze_columns(2)
widths = [8,20,48,8,12,12,28,20,10,20,40,46,14,16,14,14]
for idx,w in enumerate(widths):
    col_letter = chr(ord('A')+idx) if idx < 26 else None
    if col_letter:
        mf.get_range(f'{col_letter}:{col_letter}').format.column_width = w
try:
    mf.tables.add(f'A1:P{len(mf_data)}', True, 'ManifestTable')
except Exception:
    pass
# Data validation for queue/grade columns
try:
    mf.get_range(f'I2:I{len(mf_data)}').data_validation = {'rule': {'type': 'list', 'values': ['A','B','C','D','E']}}
    mf.get_range(f'J2:J{len(mf_data)}').data_validation = {'rule': {'type': 'list', 'values': ['implement-now','inspect-then-implement','spec-first','future-release','parked']}}
except Exception:
    pass

# Dependency additions
ds = wb.worksheets.add('Dependencies')
ds_cols = ['issue_id','depends_on_id','type','issue_release','depends_on_release','reason']
ds_data = [ds_cols] + [[d.get(c,'') for c in ds_cols] for d in deps]
ds.get_range_by_indexes(0,0,len(ds_data),len(ds_cols)).values = ds_data
ds.get_range_by_indexes(0,0,1,len(ds_cols)).format = header_fmt
ds.get_range_by_indexes(1,0,len(ds_data)-1,len(ds_cols)).format = text_fmt
ds.freeze_panes.freeze_rows(1)
for col,w in [('A',22),('B',22),('C',12),('D',30),('E',30),('F',70)]:
    ds.get_range(f'{col}:{col}').format.column_width = w
try:
    ds.tables.add(f'A1:F{len(ds_data)}', True, 'DependencyTable')
except Exception:
    pass

# AC patches
acs = wb.worksheets.add('AC_Patches')
ac_cols = ['issue_id','priority','type','release_key','title','acceptance_criteria']
ac_data = [ac_cols] + [[a.get(c,'') for c in ac_cols] for a in ac]
acs.get_range_by_indexes(0,0,len(ac_data),len(ac_cols)).values = ac_data
acs.get_range_by_indexes(0,0,1,len(ac_cols)).format = header_fmt
acs.get_range_by_indexes(1,0,len(ac_data)-1,len(ac_cols)).format = text_fmt
acs.freeze_panes.freeze_rows(1)
for col,w in [('A',22),('B',8),('C',10),('D',30),('E',50),('F',90)]:
    acs.get_range(f'{col}:{col}').format.column_width = w
try:
    acs.tables.add(f'A1:F{len(ac_data)}', True, 'AcceptancePatchTable')
except Exception:
    pass

# Packets
pk = wb.worksheets.add('Packets')
pk_cols = ['packet_id','name','primary_bead','included_beads','release_key','lane','proof_artifact','verify','rollback']
pk_data = [pk_cols] + [[p.get(c,'') for c in pk_cols] for p in packets]
pk.get_range_by_indexes(0,0,len(pk_data),len(pk_cols)).values = pk_data
pk.get_range_by_indexes(0,0,1,len(pk_cols)).format = header_fmt
pk.get_range_by_indexes(1,0,len(pk_data)-1,len(pk_cols)).format = text_fmt
pk.freeze_panes.freeze_rows(1)
for col,w in [('A',10),('B',34),('C',22),('D',48),('E',30),('F',20),('G',60),('H',60),('I',60)]:
    pk.get_range(f'{col}:{col}').format.column_width = w
try:
    pk.tables.add(f'A1:I{len(pk_data)}', True, 'PacketsTable')
except Exception:
    pass

# Formatting rows heights caps
for sname in ['Dashboard','Release_Gates','Manifest','Dependencies','AC_Patches','Packets']:
    s = wb.worksheets.get_item(sname)
    try:
        s.get_range('1:1').format.row_height = 32
    except Exception:
        pass

# Quick inspection and error scan
print(wb.inspect({'kind':'table','range':'Dashboard!A1:H20','include':'values,formulas','table_max_rows':20,'table_max_cols':8}).ndjson)
print(wb.inspect({'kind':'match','search_term':'#REF!|#DIV/0!|#VALUE!|#NAME\\?|#N/A','options':{'use_regex':True,'max_results':100},'summary':'formula error scan'}).ndjson)
SpreadsheetFile.export_xlsx(wb).save(str(OUT))
print(OUT)

bash -lc python - <<'PY'
import json,pathlib,collections,sys
B=pathlib.Path('/mnt/data/polylogue_beads_upgrade_bundle')
# load issues
issues={}
for line in pathlib.Path('/mnt/data/polylogue_extract/polylogue/polylogue-beads-export.jsonl').open():
 o=json.loads(line)
 if o.get('_type')=='issue': issues[o['id']]=o
active={}
for row in (B/'delivery_manifest.jsonl').open():
 r=json.loads(row); active[r['id']]=r
active_set=set(active)
# edges active hard blocks existing + proposed
edges=collections.defaultdict(list)
all_edges=[]
for iid in active_set:
 for d in issues[iid].get('dependencies',[]) or []:
  if d.get('type')=='blocks' and d.get('depends_on_id') in active_set:
   edges[iid].append(d['depends_on_id']); all_edges.append((iid,d['depends_on_id'],'existing'))
for line in (B/'dependency_additions.jsonl').open():
 e=json.loads(line)
 if e['issue_id'] in active_set and e['depends_on_id'] in active_set:
  edges[e['issue_id']].append(e['depends_on_id']); all_edges.append((e['issue_id'],e['depends_on_id'],'proposed'))
# cycle detection in dependency graph issue -> depends_on (cycle if path returns)
vis={}; stack=[]; cycles=[]
def dfs(n):
    vis[n]=1; stack.append(n)
    for m in edges.get(n,[]):
        if vis.get(m)==1:
            i=stack.index(m); cycles.append(stack[i:]+[m])
        elif vis.get(m,0)==0:
            dfs(m)
    stack.pop(); vis[n]=2
for n in active_set:
    if vis.get(n,0)==0: dfs(n)
print('active hard edges',len(all_edges),'cycles',len(cycles))
for c in cycles[:5]: print('cycle', ' -> '.join(c))
# JSONL validation
for fname in ['delivery_manifest.jsonl','dependency_additions.jsonl','acceptance_criteria_patches.jsonl','label_patches.jsonl','beads_upgrade_patch.jsonl','release_gates.jsonl','implementation_packets.jsonl','polylogue-beads-upgraded-candidate.jsonl']:
 c=0
 for line in (B/fname).open():
  if line.strip(): json.loads(line); c+=1
 print(fname,c)

import json,pathlib,collections
B=pathlib.Path('/mnt/data/polylogue_beads_upgrade_bundle')
issues={}
for line in pathlib.Path('/mnt/data/polylogue_extract/polylogue/polylogue-beads-export.jsonl').open():

 if o.get('_type')=='issue': issues[o['id']]=o

   edges[iid].append(d['depends_on_id'])

 if e['issue_id'] in active and e['depends_on_id'] in active:

 stack.pop(); vis[n]=2
for n in active:
 if vis.get(n,0)==0: dfs(n)

# list files sizes

 print(p.name, p.stat().st_size)

## 458. assistant

_create_time: 1783383548.578527_

Done. I turned the refined plan into a downloadable upgraded Beads setup package.

[Download the upgraded Beads setup ZIP](sandbox:/mnt/data/polylogue_beads_upgrade_setup.zip)

Key individual files:

[Patch manifest JSON](sandbox:/mnt/data/polylogue_beads_upgrade_setup/patch_manifest.json)  
[Delivery manifest CSV](sandbox:/mnt/data/polylogue_beads_upgrade_setup/delivery_manifest.csv)  
[Delivery manifest JSON](sandbox:/mnt/data/polylogue_beads_upgrade_setup/delivery_manifest.json)  
[Patched Beads export preview JSONL](sandbox:/mnt/data/polylogue_beads_upgrade_setup/patched/polylogue-beads-upgraded-export.jsonl)  
[Implementation playbook](sandbox:/mnt/data/polylogue_beads_upgrade_setup/implementation_playbook.md)  
[Release gates](sandbox:/mnt/data/polylogue_beads_upgrade_setup/release_gates.md)  
[Proposed dependency additions](sandbox:/mnt/data/polylogue_beads_upgrade_setup/dependency_additions.md)  
[Proposed acceptance-criteria fills](sandbox:/mnt/data/polylogue_beads_upgrade_setup/missing_acceptance_criteria_fills.md)

What I added/refined into the setup:

It now classifies all 397 active beads into delivery releases, lanes, readiness grades, and proof lanes.

It adds proposed acceptance criteria for all 72 active beads that lacked them, including detailed P2 fills for:

`polylogue-rsad`  
`polylogue-2qx`  
`polylogue-37t.5`  
`polylogue-rii.2`  
`polylogue-fs1.4`

It proposes 191 hard `blocks` dependency edges to make hidden delivery dependencies explicit. The important ones encode rules like: public claims wait for evidence honesty and citations; agent context waits for safe write policy and the scheduler; browser posting waits for daemon security and blob integrity; analytics wait for the measure registry and evidence semantics; interop waits for `OriginSpec`; federation waits for idempotent export/import.

It proposes 1,263 delivery labels across active beads, covering release, lane, and readiness grade.

It appends delivery notes to the active beads without replacing existing notes.

It adds 5 proposed durable Beads memories for delivery rules: gated execution, readiness definitions, public-claims discipline, agent-context safety, and origin-contract policy.

The ZIP includes a patched export-shaped JSONL preview, but I did not apply anything to a live Beads database. The authoritative file is `patch_manifest.json`; the included `scripts/apply_upgrade_to_export.py` applies the patch safely to an exported JSONL by only appending labels/notes/dependencies, adding memories when absent, and setting acceptance criteria only when the field is empty.

    if o.get('_type')=='issue': issues.append(o)

class V(ast.NodeVisitor):
 def visit_Call(self,node):
  if isinstance(node.func, ast.Name) and node.func.id=='InsightType':
   name=None
   for kw in node.keywords:
    if kw.arg=='name' and isinstance(kw.value, ast.Constant): name=kw.value.value

  self.generic_visit(node)
V().visit(ast.parse(src))

# Polylogue urgent / correctness / critical-path bead packets

This is a static handoff for coding agents. It turns selected urgent beads into concrete implementation instructions and verification lanes. It was built by reading the Beads export plus the Polylogue source tree from the uploaded archive. Paths and line numbers refer to the unpacked snapshot I inspected under `/mnt/data/work/poly/repo/polylogue`.

The ordering is intentional: first stop data loss and security hazards, then stop false evidence/memory claims, then restore temporal/evidence honesty, then unblock demonstrations and larger substrate work.

## 1. `polylogue-8jg9.4` — stop ops-doctor blob cleanup deleting leased blobs

Priority: P1. Type: correctness / data-loss.

### Mechanism found

Polylogue already has a lease-aware GC implementation, but the repair path bypasses it.

Safe path:

`polylogue/storage/blob_gc.py:7-16` states the intended invariant: never delete referenced blobs; never delete blobs with an active pending lease; age/generation gate deletion; keep batches bounded. `_has_active_lease()` at `blob_gc.py:163-169` checks `pending_blob_refs`.

Unsafe path:

`polylogue/storage/blob_store.py:352-385` implements `detect_orphans(db_referenced_ids)` as a pure “files on disk minus caller-supplied referenced hashes” operation. It does not know about `pending_blob_refs`, GC generations, age gates, or archive DB state.

`polylogue/storage/blob_store.py:387-450` implements `cleanup_orphans(orphan_hashes, dry_run=False)` and destructively calls `blob_path.unlink()` after validating the hash/path.

`polylogue/storage/blob_repair.py:92-122` calls `detect_orphans`, recomputes `orphan_hashes = {h for h in iter_all() if h not in referenced_hashes}`, and then calls `cleanup_orphans`. That means an in-flight blob that has been written to disk and leased in `pending_blob_refs`, but has not yet landed in `raw_sessions` or `blob_refs`, is invisible to the repair path and may be deleted.

Normal `run_blob_gc()` would preserve it; ops-doctor repair does not.

### Implementation instructions

Retire the destructive repair path as an independent deleter. `repair_orphaned_blobs_data()` should delegate deletion to the lease-aware GC layer, probably by constructing a `BlobGCConfig` and calling `run_blob_gc_report()` / `run_blob_gc()`.

Keep `BlobStore.detect_orphans()` only as a diagnostic candidate detector, and rename or document it as “raw disk-minus-reference candidates,” not “safe to delete.” Do not let `BlobStore.cleanup_orphans(dry_run=False)` be reachable from operator repair unless the caller has already run the lease/generation/age checks.

`polylogue ops doctor` should report: referenced count, raw candidate count, safe-delete count, skipped because leased, skipped because too new, skipped because generation boundary, deleted count.

### Tests to add

Create a temporary archive DB with the needed tables: `raw_sessions`, `blob_refs`, `pending_blob_refs`, and `gc_generations`. Write a blob file, insert only a `pending_blob_refs` lease, then run the repair/doctor cleanup in non-dry-run mode. The blob must survive and the report must say it was skipped because leased.

Add the positive control: an old unleased, unreferenced blob is deleted only after the generation/age gate is satisfied.

### Verification

Run:

```bash
python -m pytest \
  tests/unit/storage/test_blob_gc.py \
  tests/unit/storage/test_blob_gc_lease_recovery.py \
  tests/unit/storage/test_blob_store_contracts.py \
  tests/unit/storage/test_blob_store.py -q
```

Then run the relevant doctor/blob integrity tests and confirm the repair command never calls raw `cleanup_orphans()` without the safe GC layer.

---

## 2. `polylogue-kwsb.1` — daemon and browser-capture Host/Origin/token/spool hardening

Priority: P1. Type: security / privacy.

### Mechanism found

Daemon HTTP:

`polylogue/daemon/http.py:1184-1185` returns 405 for `OPTIONS`, matching the documented no-CORS stance.

`polylogue/daemon/http.py:1191-1251` dispatches GET requests. Some routes are intentionally unauthenticated local shell/status routes, and authenticated routes are optionally protected by bearer token, but there is no central Host admission check before GET routing.

`polylogue/daemon/http.py:1294-1297` parses the path and dispatches GET directly.

`polylogue/daemon/http.py:1301-1313` has an Origin check, but it is used for POST/DELETE. GET is the dangerous gap because browsers can issue GETs cross-site and DNS rebinding attacks target Host semantics.

Browser capture:

`polylogue/browser_capture/server.py:54-61` allows missing Origin.

`polylogue/browser_capture/server.py:68-73` returns true when `auth_token is None`; the receiver is unauthenticated by default.

`polylogue/browser_capture/server.py:241-283` caps each POST body at 128 MiB, but there is no total spool governor before writing artifacts.

`polylogue/browser_capture/server.py:385-409` constructs the server with `auth_token=None` by default.

### Implementation instructions

Add one central Host admission helper and invoke it before all daemon request dispatch, including GET, POST, DELETE, and any future route. For loopback binds, accept only loopback Host authorities: `localhost`, `localhost:<port>`, `127.0.0.1`, `127.*`, `[::1]`, and the configured loopback host/port. Reject missing or hostile Host on HTTP/1.1 requests where the header is expected.

Add GET Origin protection. If a GET has an Origin header, it must be same-origin/allowed-loopback. Missing Origin is acceptable only if Host is admitted. Keep `OPTIONS = 405`; do not add CORS.

Apply the same Host admission to the browser-capture receiver.

Make browser-capture bearer auth effectively required. If the operator does not supply `--browser-capture-auth-token`, mint or load a stable random token from a mode-0600 file under the browser-capture state/spool root. The extension install/status path should expose the token through the intended local operator channel, not logs or URLs. Use `hmac.compare_digest` for token comparison.

Add a spool governor to the browser capture config: maximum total spool bytes, maximum artifact files, and clear rejection before partial writes. Per-request `Content-Length` checks are not enough.

### Tests to add

Daemon:

A GET to `/api/sessions` or another read route with `Host: evil.example` must be refused even if no Origin is present.

A GET with `Host: localhost:<port>` and no Origin must preserve existing behavior.

A GET with good Host and evil Origin must be refused.

The web shell/status routes should remain available only under admitted Host.

Browser capture:

No-token default should not mean unauthenticated acceptance. Missing token is refused unless the test explicitly opts into an unsafe/test mode.

Good token succeeds. Bad token fails. Hostile Host fails. Spool-full fails without partial artifact writes.

### Verification

Run:

```bash
python -m pytest \
  tests/unit/daemon/test_daemon_http_security.py \
  tests/unit/daemon/test_daemon_cli_remote_bind.py -q

python -m pytest \
  tests/unit/browser_capture \
  tests/unit/daemon/test_daemon_cli.py \
  tests/unit/daemon/test_metrics_endpoint.py \
  tests/unit/daemon/test_healthz.py -q
```

Also manually inspect docs and tests to ensure the explicit security decisions still hold: raw artifacts are operator-trust endpoints, `/api/sources` exposes absolute paths to authenticated callers, no CORS preflight is supported, and browser capture has a separate token model.

---

## 3. `polylogue-37t.15` — force non-user assertions through candidate/non-injected policy

Priority: P1. Type: memory safety / agent safety.

### Mechanism found

`polylogue/storage/sqlite/archive_tiers/user_write.py:31-35` has default assertion write parameters that are active/user-shaped.

`upsert_blackboard_note()` at `user_write.py:641-671` forwards `author_kind` and context policy into `upsert_assertion()`.

`upsert_assertion()` at `user_write.py:901-999` trusts caller-supplied `author_kind`, `status`, and `context_policy`. It also updates existing rows on conflict.

`judge_assertion_candidate()` at `user_write.py:1245-1320` already models the intended explicit user-judgment path.

`polylogue/mcp/server_mutation_tools.py:140-180` exposes `blackboard_post` through MCP and defaults `author_kind` to `agent`.

The chokepoint exists but does not enforce policy. An agent-authored blackboard post can become an active assertion if the caller or defaults produce active/injecting state.

### Implementation instructions

Implement the safety policy inside `upsert_assertion()`, not only in MCP handlers.

If `author_kind == "user"`, preserve existing behavior.

If `author_kind != "user"`, force:

- `status = CANDIDATE`
- `context_policy.inject = False`
- `promotion_required = True` or equivalent metadata
- provenance records the original requested status/policy if useful for debugging

When upserting an existing assertion, first read its current status and context policy. If the existing status is terminally judged, especially `REJECTED`, `DEFERRED`, or `SUPERSEDED`, an agent re-upsert must not resurrect it into active/candidate/injected state. User judgment remains the promotion path.

Do not add a trusted-agent bypass unless the bead explicitly introduces one later. The safe default is all non-user writes are candidates.

### Tests to add

Direct storage test: `upsert_assertion(author_kind="agent", status=ACTIVE, inject=True)` writes a candidate with no injection.

Blackboard test: `upsert_blackboard_note(author_kind="agent")` writes candidate/no-inject.

MCP mutation test: default `blackboard_post` writes candidate/no-inject.

User test: `author_kind="user"` active/inject behavior remains intact.

Judgment test: an agent cannot re-upsert a rejected candidate into active or injected status.

### Verification

Run:

```bash
python -m pytest \
  tests/unit/storage/test_archive_tiers_assertions.py \
  tests/unit/storage/test_archive_tiers_assertion_write_through.py \
  tests/unit/storage/test_archive_tiers_user_write.py \
  tests/unit/storage/test_blackboard_facade.py \
  tests/unit/mcp -q -k 'assertion or blackboard'
```

Then search for direct assertion writes outside the storage chokepoint:

```bash
rg "upsert_assertion|INSERT INTO assertions|blackboard_post" polylogue tests
```

## 4. `polylogue-cpf.6` — add a clock seam and audit `sort_key_ms`

Priority: P1. Type: temporal correctness / reproducibility.

### Mechanism found

`polylogue/core/dates.py:10-44` implements `parse_date()` with a hardcoded `datetime.now(timezone.utc)`.

`polylogue/archive/query/spec.py:136-142` calls `parse_date()` through `parse_query_date()` without a clock seam.

`polylogue/archive/query/spec.py:497-505` builds `SessionQuerySpec.from_params()` without any way to pass a frozen clock.

`polylogue/archive/filter/builder.py:107-119` parses date strings directly.

`polylogue/storage/insights/session/rebuild.py:107-111` orders using `COALESCE(sort_key_ms, 0)` and `source_sort_key`.

`rebuild.py:1153-1177` uses `int(row["sort_key_ms"] or 0)` and then uses `source_sort_key_ms=sort_key_by_session.get(session_id) or hwm_ms`. This conflates missing, zero, and fallback.

`polylogue/storage/insights/session/status.py` uses several `COALESCE(c.sort_key_ms,0)` expressions in freshness/readiness comparisons.

### Implementation instructions

Add a clock seam:

```python
def parse_date(date_str: str, *, now: datetime | None = None) -> datetime:
    base = now or datetime.now(timezone.utc)
```

Thread the seam through `parse_query_date()`, `SessionQuerySpec.from_params()`, and filter builder construction. Every relative date in one query should share the same base instant.

Audit `sort_key_ms` use. Do not convert unknown sort keys to epoch zero for freshness or evidence provenance. For ordering, use explicit null ordering: known timestamps first, newest first, timeless/unknown last. In SQL that is usually:

```sql
ORDER BY sort_key_ms IS NULL ASC, sort_key_ms DESC
```

In Python, avoid `x or fallback` for timestamps because valid zero and missing collapse. Use `is None` tests.

Commit `docs/audits/sort-key-ms-audit.md` or a similar generated/static audit file that lists every `sort_key_ms` use and classifies it as ordering, freshness, display, fallback, or bug-fixed.

### Tests to add

Frozen relative-date tests: `parse_date("yesterday", now=frozen)` and `SessionQuerySpec.from_params(since="yesterday", now=frozen)` produce deterministic bounds.

Single-query consistency test: `since="last week"` and `until="today"` use the same injected `now`.

Null sort-key tests: a session with no provider/capture timestamp must not appear as epoch-stale; it orders after known sessions and carries weak/unknown temporal provenance.

### Verification

Run:

```bash
python -m pytest \
  tests/unit/core/test_dates.py \
  tests/unit/archive/test_query_spec.py \
  tests/unit/archive/test_query_expression.py \
  tests/unit/storage/test_session_insight_rebuild*.py \
  tests/unit/storage/test_session_insight_status*.py -q

rg "parse_date\(|COALESCE\([^\n]*sort_key|sort_key_ms.*or 0|source_sort_key_ms=.*or" polylogue tests
```

The final `rg` should show only intentional audited uses.

## 5. `polylogue-cpf.5` — propagate weakest temporal provenance through aggregates

Priority: P1. Type: evidence honesty.

### Mechanism found

`polylogue/insights/temporal_source.py:17-39` has a useful timestamp-source taxonomy.

`temporal_source.py:66-81` implements `classify_profile_hwm_source(updated_at)` as provider timestamp whenever `updated_at` is non-null.

`temporal_source.py:97-108` implements `classify_aggregate_hwm_source(source_updates)` as provider timestamp whenever the aggregate has any update value.

`polylogue/insights/archive_summaries.py` and `archive_rollups.py` pass timestamp strings rather than timestamp-source classes.

`polylogue/storage/insights/session/profiles.py` and `timeline_rows.py` have profile/timeline evidence paths but do not consistently propagate the profile timestamp-source evidence into aggregates.

Existing tests already indicate fallback source states exist: `tests/unit/storage/test_session_insight_refresh.py:500` and `tests/unit/storage/test_session_insight_profiles.py:464-482` cover fallback-style timestamp evidence.

### Implementation instructions

Define an explicit strength lattice. Example strongest to weakest:

1. `provider_ts`
2. `hook_event_ts`
3. `sort_key`
4. `file_mtime`
5. `materialization_ts`
6. `fallback_date`
7. `unknown`

`classify_aggregate_hwm_source()` must consume source classes, not just timestamp strings, and return the weakest present class. A mixed aggregate containing provider timestamps and fallback dates is fallback-derived, not provider-derived.

`classify_profile_hwm_source()` should accept the profile’s actual timestamp-source signal. A non-null `updated_at` with `session_timestamp_fallback` is still fallback-derived.

Thread timestamp-source values through profile reads, timeline rows, session summaries, day/week rollups, archive rollups, and any public JSON/report fields that summarize time ranges.

### Tests to add

Unit lattice tests:

- provider + fallback => fallback
- provider + file_mtime => file_mtime
- empty/unknown => unknown or fallback, not provider

Profile test: non-null `updated_at` plus `session_timestamp_fallback` stores/returns fallback.

Aggregate test: a day/week/product aggregate over one provider timestamp and one fallback timestamp renders the aggregate time provenance as fallback.

### Verification

Run:

```bash
python -m pytest \
  tests/unit/insights/test_temporal_source_taxonomy.py \
  tests/unit/storage/test_session_insight_profiles.py \
  tests/unit/storage/test_session_insight_refresh.py \
  tests/unit/insights/test_archive_rollups.py \
  tests/unit/insights/test_archive_summaries.py -q
```

Then inspect JSON/report snapshots to ensure the caveat survives rendering.

## 6. `polylogue-9e5.28` — rigor audit must cover the product registry

Priority: P1. Type: evidence-honesty gate.

### Mechanism found

`polylogue/insights/registry.py:294-300` exposes `INSIGHT_REGISTRY` / `list_insight_products()`. In the inspected snapshot the registered products include at least:

- `session_profiles`
- `session_work_events`
- `session_phases`
- `threads`
- `session_tag_rollups`
- `archive_coverage`
- `tool_usage`
- `session_costs`
- `cost_rollups`
- `usage_timeline`
- `archive_debt`

`polylogue/insights/rigor.py:85-210` declares rigor contracts for only a subset.

`polylogue/insights/audit.py:173-183` documents that products without rigor contracts are skipped.

`audit.py:185-201` iterates only `list_rigor_contracts()`.

So the audit can pass while registered products have no rigor contract. The bead’s phrasing matches the actual mechanism.

### Implementation instructions

Change the audit’s primary loop to iterate the insight product registry, not the contract registry.

For each product:

- If a rigor contract exists, audit normally.
- If the product has an explicit exemption, emit an `exempt` entry with reason, owner, and expiry/revisit bead where possible.
- If neither exists, emit an `uncovered` entry. This should fail the strict audit lane.

Add a `coverage_status` field to audit entries: `covered`, `exempt`, `uncovered`, maybe `unknown` for migration.

Then either add contracts or explicit exemptions for all current registry products. Because most uncovered products are number-bearing, prefer real contracts over exemptions.

### Tests to add

Registry parity test: the audit emits one entry per `INSIGHT_REGISTRY` product.

Temporary product test: monkeypatch/register a product with no contract; strict audit fails and reports `uncovered`.

Exemption test: a product with explicit exemption appears in output and does not silently vanish.

CLI/API rendering test: uncovered products are visible in text and JSON.

### Verification

Run:

```bash
python -m pytest \
  tests/unit/insights/test_rigor_audit.py \
  tests/unit/cli/test_insights.py \
  tests/unit/api/test_facade_contracts.py \
  tests/unit/core/test_insight_registry_parity.py \
  tests/unit/insights/test_registry.py -q
```

Manual acceptance: `polylogue insights rigor` or equivalent output must list all registered products.

## 7. `polylogue-9e5.29` — prevent numeric zero claims over absent evidence

Priority: P1. Type: evidence honesty / report correctness.

### Mechanism found

The current rigor model is mostly product-level. Numeric fields do not appear to have field-level absence semantics. Several surfaces and derived SQL paths use ordinary count/default/COALESCE patterns, which are safe only when the denominator is known and coverage exists.

This bead is less about one single line and more about a missing contract class: a number is not trustworthy unless the system knows whether it is a true zero, absent evidence, uncovered source, not applicable, or unknown.

### Implementation instructions

Extend the rigor/audit model with field-level numeric contracts. A minimal contract shape:

```python
@dataclass(frozen=True)
class RigorFieldContract:
    field_path: str
    kind: Literal["count", "duration", "cost", "tokens", "rate", "ratio", "score"]
    unit: str | None
    denominator: str | None
    true_zero_when: str
    absent_when: str
    nullable_when_uncovered: bool = True
```

Attach these to `RigorContract`.

The audit should inspect product schemas/registry metadata/renderers and report uncontracted numeric fields.

Policy:

- No backing rows and no coverage denominator => `None` / `unknown` / `uncovered`, never `0`.
- Covered source with denominator and no events => true zero is allowed.
- Not applicable is distinct from unknown.
- Rendered human text may say `unknown` or `uncovered`; JSON should use `null` plus caveat/status fields.

Start with the high-risk products: `archive_coverage`, `tool_usage`, `session_costs`, `cost_rollups`, `usage_timeline`, `archive_debt`, work-event durations, phase counts, thread counts, and session-profile evidence counts.

### Tests to add

No-data test: an empty or unmaterialized backing table must not render a zero count/rate.

Covered-zero test: a covered source with zero matching events may render zero and must include the coverage denominator.

CLI/JSON tests: human output says unknown/uncovered; JSON uses null plus status/caveat.

Audit test: adding a numeric field without a field contract fails strict rigor.

### Verification

Run:

```bash
python -m pytest \
  tests/unit/insights/test_rigor_audit.py \
  tests/unit/cli/test_insights.py \
  tests/unit/api/test_facade_contracts.py \
  tests/unit/insights/test_registry.py -q

rg "default=\"0\"|return \"0\"| or 0\)| or 0\b|COALESCE\([^\n]*, 0" polylogue tests
```

Every remaining zero default should be audited as either true-zero-safe or internal-only.

---

## 8. `polylogue-9e5.30` — tag prose-mined forensic fields as text-derived

Priority: P1. Type: provenance honesty.

### Mechanism found

`polylogue/insights/transforms.py:77-86` defines regexes used to mine test commands, commit refs, and related facts from text.

`ToolSummary` at `transforms.py:192-205`, `SubagentReport` at `214-228`, and `DecisionCandidate` at `280-292` carry mined fields but no per-field provenance.

`_tool_bundle_metadata()` at `transforms.py:1272-1275` renders mined `commit_refs` and `test_evidence`.

`_extract_decision_candidates()` at `transforms.py:1923-1951` mines decision-like prose.

`_test_evidence()` at `transforms.py:2178` and `_tool_commit_refs()` at `2257` extract structured-looking fields from text.

The forensic index can therefore display fields that look like structured facts even though they were mined from prose/tool output.

### Implementation instructions

Add explicit provenance for mined fields. The low-friction implementation is a `text_derived_fields: dict[str, TextDerivedProvenance]` on `ToolSummary`, `SubagentReport`, `DecisionCandidate`, and forensic index entries. A richer implementation can wrap each field.

Provenance should include source kind: `assistant_prose`, `tool_output`, `command_text`, `regex`, extractor version, source span/ref where available, and confidence if already available.

When `_test_evidence()` or `_tool_commit_refs()` populates fields, it must add provenance. Decision candidates mined from prose must render as candidate interpretations, not external ground truth.

Reports and JSON should expose the caveat. A readable form:

`text-derived(tool_output): commit_refs, test_evidence`

### Tests to add

A tool output containing `pytest ...` produces `test_evidence` and marks it text-derived.

A prose “we decided X” produces a `DecisionCandidate` marked text-derived.

Markdown and JSON reports include the caveat.

No test should treat mined commit refs as equivalent to verified git commits unless a separate git evidence join confirms them.

### Verification

Run:

```bash
python -m pytest \
  tests/unit/insights/test_transforms.py \
  tests/unit/cli/test_context_image_view.py \
  tests/unit/mcp/test_envelope_contracts.py -q
```

Then search for mined fields that are not listed in `text_derived_fields`.

## 9. `polylogue-83u.3` — preserve uploaded attachment bytes in live browser capture

Priority: P1. Type: evidence completeness / blob integrity.

### Mechanism found

`polylogue/browser_capture/models.py:22-34` allows capture attachments to carry inline bytes through fields such as `inline_base64`, `content_base64`, and `data`.

`polylogue/sources/parsers/browser_capture.py:83-132` has a fallback parser path that decodes those inline bytes into `ParsedAttachment.inline_bytes`.

`polylogue/storage/sqlite/archive_tiers/write.py:4121-4138` writes `ParsedAttachment.inline_bytes` into the blob store and records acquired hashes/status.

The likely bug is in the native-payload fast path:

`browser_capture.py:140-152` returns the native provider parser result when `raw_provider_payload` is present. That happens before the fallback attachment loop. `_apply_browser_capture_session_kind()` at `browser_capture.py:59-68` changes session kind/provenance flags but does not merge envelope-level attachment bytes into the native parsed session.

So a ChatGPT/Claude native payload captured with inline attachment bytes in the browser envelope can preserve the transcript while dropping the envelope-provided bytes.

### Implementation instructions

Implement a helper such as `_browser_capture_envelope_attachments(envelope)` that normalizes envelope attachments into `ParsedAttachment` values with inline bytes.

Modify `_apply_browser_capture_session_kind()` or the native fast path to merge envelope attachment bytes into the native parser result before returning.

Deduplicate by the strongest stable keys available:

- provider attachment id
- message provider id
- filename + size + content hash

If the native parser emits attachment metadata but no bytes, fill in `inline_bytes` from the envelope. If the native parser already has bytes, do not duplicate.

Preserve fallback DOM behavior unchanged.

### Tests to add

Native ChatGPT/Claude payload plus browser-capture envelope inline attachment must result in a persisted blob with `acquisition_status = acquired` and the expected SHA-256.

Same payload without inline bytes remains metadata-only.

Duplicate envelope/native references do not create duplicate attachment rows.

### Verification

Run:

```bash
python -m pytest \
  tests/unit/sources/test_browser_capture_parser.py \
  tests/unit/sources/test_live_batch_support.py \
  tests/visual/test_reader_attachments.py -q
```

Also run blob integrity tests if the writer path changes.

## 11. `polylogue-b5l` — blue-green derived-tier rebuilds

Priority: P2, but critical path for safe scale. Type: storage architecture.

### Mechanism/design advanced

Polylogue’s architecture splits durable source/user tiers from derived index/embedding tiers. The target rebuild behavior should respect that split: source evidence remains authoritative, while derived indexes are rebuilt beside the live generation and swapped only after verification.

### Implementation instructions

Introduce generation-managed derived tiers.

Suggested filesystem shape:

```text
archive_root/
  index-current.json
  index-generations/
    20260707T.../
      index.db
      manifest.json
      verify.json
```

`index-current.json` or equivalent points to the serving generation. Readers open the serving generation, not a hardcoded `index.db`. Writers/convergence stages build into a new generation.

Generation states:

- `building`
- `catching_up`
- `verified`
- `serving`
- `retired`
- `failed`

A rebuild flow:

1. Create generation directory.
2. Build derived DB from durable `source.db` / `user.db`.
3. Capture source high-water mark and write queue position.
4. Replay or fence writes that happened during build.
5. Verify schema, source HWM, FTS coverage, insight readiness, and blob reference sanity.
6. Atomic pointer swap using temp file + fsync + rename.
7. Keep old generation until a retire policy reaps it.

Status surfaces must say “serving old generation while building new generation,” not “archive ready” over a partial derived DB.

### Tests to add

Reader keeps using old generation while a new generation is building.

Failed build does not move the pointer.

Successful build swaps pointer atomically.

A write during rebuild is either replayed into the new generation or produces a clear blocked/degraded state.

Status JSON exposes serving/building generation ids and progress.

### Verification

Run:

```bash
python -m pytest \
  tests/unit/storage \
  tests/unit/daemon/test_daemon_status.py \
  tests/unit/daemon/test_convergence_stages.py \
  tests/unit/sources/test_live_batch_support.py -q

rg "active_index_db_path|index.db|schema version|FTS invariant|session_insight_readiness" polylogue tests
```

---

## 12. `polylogue-s7ae.6` — classify aborted full verify before coordination deploy

Priority: P1. Type: release gate / trust.

### Mechanism/design advanced

This bead cannot be fully resolved statically because the important evidence is the aborted full-verify log and current runtime state. The coding-agent work can still be made precise.

### Implementation instructions

Create a durable classification artifact:

```text
.agent/reports/verify-classification/<timestamp>-coordination-full-verify.md
```

It must contain:

- commit SHA
- dirty tree state
- exact command
- environment summary
- start/end timestamps
- abort reason
- last completed phase
- stdout/stderr artifact paths
- every failed lane/test/check
- classification per failure

Allowed classifications:

- `coordination_regression`
- `pre_existing`
- `environmental`
- `flaky`
- `intentional_defer`
- `unknown_blocker`

Unknown blockers fail the gate.

If `devtools verify` does not already emit a phase ledger, add one minimally: phase name, start/end, exit, captured log path.

```bash
devtools verify 2>&1 | tee .agent/reports/verify-classification/<timestamp>/full-verify.log
```

Then run focused tests for any devtools classification/reporting change:

```bash
python -m pytest tests/unit/devtools/test_task_history.py tests/unit/devtools/test_verify*.py -q
```

Acceptance: every failure is classified and linked to a bead, fix commit, or explicit pre-existing evidence. Coordination deploy remains blocked until no unknown blockers remain.

## 13. `polylogue-4smp` / `polylogue-0v9p` / `polylogue-arso` / `polylogue-rlsb` / `polylogue-d4zk` — content variants

Priority: P1/P2 cluster. Type: product substrate / evidence integrity.

### Static state

The current codebase has message-level `variant_index`-style metadata and language hints, but no first-class content-variant substrate with separate variant identity, nodes, alignment, and review lifecycle. This should be implemented as a substrate feature, not as renderer-side copied text.

### Implementation order

1. `polylogue-0v9p`: language detection and preference facts.
2. `polylogue-arso`: variant refs, nodes, alignment, storage.
3. `polylogue-rlsb`: variant-aware projection, query, and reader render profiles.
4. `polylogue-d4zk`: user/agent UX for creating, reviewing, and messaging about variants.
5. `polylogue-4smp`: epic closure only after the above compose.

### Implementation instructions

Add first-class tables/models:

```text
content_variants(
  variant_id,
  source_ref,
  kind,
  language,
  status,
  author_kind,
  provenance,
  created_at,
  updated_at
)

content_variant_nodes(
  node_id,
  variant_id,
  source_ref,
  grain,
  text,
  text_hash,
  order_index,
  metadata_json
)

content_variant_alignment(
  alignment_id,
  variant_node_id,
  source_ref,
  relation,
  confidence,
  metadata_json
)
```

Variant kinds should be closed vocabulary at first: translation, transliteration, simplification, summary.

Alignment relations should cover one-to-one, one-to-many, many-to-one, omitted, expanded, reordered, and partial.

Do not overwrite source content or source content hashes. Variants are transformed views, not original evidence.

Projection profiles:

- `source`
- `preferred`
- `side_by_side`
- `variant:<id>`

Agent-created variants must obey `polylogue-37t.15`: candidate/reviewed, non-injected by default.

### Tests to add

Mixed-language fixture: raw source stays unchanged; translation and simplification variants attach to it.

Alignment fixture: one-to-many and omitted mappings survive storage and rendering.

Query fixture: searching variant text returns source refs with a transformed-content caveat.

Citation fixture: reports cite original source plus optional variant view; they do not cite a translation as original text.

Agent fixture: agent-created variant is candidate/review-required.

### Verification

Run:

```bash
python -m pytest tests/unit/storage tests/unit/archive tests/unit/cli tests/unit/mcp -q -k 'variant or language or assertion'
```

Also add generated schema/docs snapshots if this repo requires them for storage changes.

# General coding-agent operating rule

For every packet above, the agent should leave a small handoff artifact under `.agent/reports/` containing:

- bead id
- source files changed
- tests run
- tests not run and why
- migration/schema notes
- remaining risks
- exact verification command output path

Do not close a parent/epic bead until children are closed or explicitly split out.

## 14. `polylogue-s7ae.5` — live proof with two agents in separate worktrees

Priority: P1. Type: coordination proof / critical demo.

### Mechanism found

The current coordination envelope has useful primitives, but the specific live proof would not be reliable yet.

`polylogue/coordination/envelope.py:36-44` defines process and resource scan constants. `_process_payloads()` at `458-531` discovers peer agents from `ps` and uses `/proc/<pid>/cwd` through `_proc_cwd()`.

The overlap detector at `1154-1188` only treats a peer as same-repo when `peer.cwd.startswith(repo.root)`.

That misses the exact proof case in the bead: two agents in separate worktrees of the same Git repository. Sibling worktrees have different `git rev-parse --show-toplevel` roots, so the peer CWD does not start with the current root. The current code detects nested same-root peers, not same Git common-dir peers.

The same code also does not compute changed-path intersection with peer agents; it only reports same-repo peer count and generic resource episodes.

### Implementation instructions

Extend `CoordinationPeerPayload` with repo identity fields:

- `repo_root`
- `git_common_dir` or normalized repository identity
- `branch`
- `head`
- `dirty`
- `changed_paths`, bounded

When a peer CWD is available, run Git probes against that CWD with the same timeout-bounded runner:

```bash
git -C <peer_cwd> rev-parse --show-toplevel
git -C <peer_cwd> rev-parse --git-common-dir
git -C <peer_cwd> branch --show-current
git -C <peer_cwd> status --porcelain=v1
```

Normalize `--git-common-dir` to an absolute path. For worktrees, this is the stable same-repository identity; if not available, fall back to origin URL + repo name + maybe `.git` realpath.

Change overlap detection:

- `same-repo-agent`: current and peer have same Git common-dir, even if worktree roots differ.
- `same-worktree-agent`: current root equals peer root.
- `changed-path-overlap`: same repo and intersecting paths after normalizing relative paths to the repository root/common path model.
- `generated-surface-overlap`: optional heuristic for `schemas/`, generated docs, OpenAPI, CLI reference, migrations.

The live proof should emit a JSON envelope containing two worktree roots, same common repo identity, at least one overlap, one scoped message/advisory, and one generated handoff ref.

### Tests to add

Fake runner test: current root `/tmp/repo-a`, peer cwd `/tmp/repo-b`, both return the same `--git-common-dir`. Envelope must report same-repo-agent.

Changed-path test: peer changed `polylogue/mcp/server_tools.py`, current changed the same path; envelope reports warning overlap with that path.

Negative test: same process command name but different Git common-dir does not report same-repo-agent.

### Verification

Run:

```bash
python -m pytest tests/unit/coordination/test_envelope.py -q
```

Manual proof command should create and preserve before/after JSON artifacts for two worktrees.

---

## 15. `polylogue-s7ae.3` — coordination messages and scheduler-mediated advisories

Priority: P1. Type: coordination substrate.

### Mechanism found

The current envelope has `advisories: tuple[str, ...]` on `AgentCoordinationPayload` and `_advisories()` at `polylogue/coordination/envelope.py:1190-1205`, but these are ephemeral strings computed from current state. There is no visible durable coordination-message model, no scoped message store, and no delivery ledger.

The result is enough for status output, but not enough for the bead’s target: “one scoped message sent, scheduler-mediated injection, handoff packet produced.” A message that matters to another agent needs identity, scope, recipient/matching policy, delivery state, expiry, evidence refs, and an injection decision.

### Implementation instructions

Add a small durable message model. Preferred location is `user.db` if messages are operator-authored/work-state, or `ops.db` if they are disposable coordination runtime. Given the bead wants evidence-backed handoffs, use durable user/work-state tables unless there is a stronger existing state store.

Minimal table shape:

```text
coordination_messages(
  message_id TEXT PRIMARY KEY,
  created_at_ms INTEGER NOT NULL,
  author_kind TEXT NOT NULL,
  author_session_ref TEXT,
  scope_kind TEXT NOT NULL,         -- repo, worktree, bead, path, session, branch
  scope_ref TEXT NOT NULL,
  severity TEXT NOT NULL,           -- info, warning, blocking
  body TEXT NOT NULL,
  evidence_refs_json TEXT NOT NULL DEFAULT '[]',
  expires_at_ms INTEGER,
  status TEXT NOT NULL DEFAULT 'active'
)

coordination_message_deliveries(
  message_id TEXT NOT NULL,
  target_session_ref TEXT NOT NULL,
  delivered_at_ms INTEGER,
  injected_at_ms INTEGER,
  delivery_state TEXT NOT NULL,
  reason TEXT,
  PRIMARY KEY (message_id, target_session_ref)
)
```

Add read/query helpers that take current coordination envelope and return matching active messages. Matching should be conservative: same Git common-dir, same bead, path overlap, same branch, or explicit session target. Expired/superseded messages must not inject.

Envelope output should include matching messages as structured payloads, not only prose advisories.

Do not inject directly from message creation. Message creation records intent; the context scheduler decides delivery.

### Tests to add

Message scoped to same repo appears in peer envelope.

Message scoped to different repo does not appear.

Expired message does not appear.

Delivery ledger records considered/not-injected/injected with reason.

An agent-authored message cannot become a trusted assertion unless routed through the assertion candidate policy from `polylogue-37t.15`.

### Verification

Run:

```bash
python -m pytest tests/unit/coordination tests/unit/context tests/unit/storage -q -k 'coordination or message or scheduler or assertion'
```

---

## 16. `polylogue-37t.11` — context scheduler: one arbiter for agent context

Priority: P1. Type: context safety / agent substrate.

### Mechanism found

`polylogue/context/compiler.py` is explicitly not a scheduler. Its module docstring says it is a thin compiler and “does not introduce a durable memory store or a new handoff ontology.”

`ContextSpec` and `ContextImage` compile bounded context images. `ContextSnapshotRecord` records delivered context. `context_snapshot_record_from_image()` is tested in `tests/unit/context/test_compiler.py` as an explicit delivery boundary.

That is good substrate, but it is not yet the bead’s “one arbiter for everything that enters an agent’s context.” MCP tools, hooks, handoffs, assertions, variants, and coordination advisories can still grow separate inclusion logic unless a scheduler owns the policy.

### Implementation instructions

Create a scheduler layer above the compiler, not inside it. Suggested module:

`polylogue/context/scheduler.py`

Core model:

```python
class ContextCandidate:
    candidate_id: str
    kind: Literal['assertion','coordination_message','handoff','query_result','variant','session_ref','warning']
    object_ref: ObjectRef | None
    evidence_refs: tuple[EvidenceRef, ...]
    trust_class: Literal['user','accepted','candidate','agent','derived','text_derived']
    freshness_ms: int | None
    priority: int
    estimated_tokens: int
    policy_tags: tuple[str, ...]

class ContextDecision:
    candidate_id: str
    action: Literal['include','omit','defer']
    reason: str
    budget_before: int
    budget_after: int
```

Scheduler inputs:

- current repo/work item/agent envelope
- requested purpose and budget
- accepted user assertions
- candidate assertions only if explicitly allowed
- active coordination messages
- handoff refs
- fresh relevant sessions/query packs
- variants/preference facts only through variant policy

Scheduler output:

- deterministic ordered candidates
- compiled `ContextImage`
- decision ledger: included, omitted, reasons, token budget
- `ContextSnapshotRecord` for actual delivery

Every SessionStart/handoff/MCP context-injection path should call scheduler first. The compiler remains a renderer/assembler.

### Tests to add

Determinism: same inputs produce byte-identical decisions and context image.

Safety: candidate assertions and agent-authored messages are omitted by default unless profile allows them.

Budget: high-priority accepted user assertion outranks low-priority large session excerpt.

Freshness: expired coordination message omitted with reason.

Ledger: every considered candidate has exactly one decision.

### Verification

Run:

```bash
python -m pytest tests/unit/context tests/unit/mcp tests/unit/storage -q -k 'context or scheduler or assertion or coordination'
```

---

## 17. `polylogue-d1y` — one-command hooks install and hook liveness monitoring

Priority: P1. Type: live substrate / adoption.

### Static state

The docs already identify hooks as central. `docs/hooks.md` describes `polylogue-hook <event-type>` and names high-value Claude/Codex events such as `SessionStart`, `UserPromptSubmit`, `PreToolUse`, `PostToolUse`, `PostToolUseFailure`, `Notification`, `CwdChanged`, and `Stop`.

The codebase contains `contrib/polylogue-hook`, `packaging/polylogue-hooks/`, hook-event tests, and hook-paste enrichment. The coordination envelope also reads Beads hook state through `bd hooks list --json`, but that is Beads hooks, not Polylogue agent hooks.

What is not yet obviously present is a one-command agent-hook installer plus liveness monitor that can say: installed for Claude Code/Codex, last event received, last event parsed, last event materialized, stale/missing/outdated.

### Implementation instructions

Add a command such as:

```bash
polylogue hooks install --target claude-code --target codex --dry-run
polylogue hooks status --json
polylogue hooks doctor
```

Install should:

- detect target config locations
- write or update hook config idempotently
- preserve existing user hooks through chaining/wrapping
- install `polylogue-hook` path from the active build
- create/update a stable hook token if needed
- dry-run with diff
- refuse unsafe overwrite unless `--force`

Status should report:

- configured target
- installed events
- hook command path
- version/hash
- last sidecar event time
- last daemon ingest time
- last archive materialization time
- stale/outdated/missing state

Liveness monitor should use event evidence, not just file existence. A hook that exists but has not emitted `SessionStart` or `UserPromptSubmit` recently should be stale.

### Tests to add

Installer preserves existing hook config and chains Polylogue.

Installer is idempotent.

Status distinguishes missing config, installed-but-never-fired, fired-but-not-ingested, and ingested/materialized.

Dry-run does not write.

### Verification

Run:

```bash
python -m pytest tests/unit/sources/test_hook_events.py tests/unit/sources/test_hook_paste_enrichment.py tests/unit/cli -q -k 'hook or hooks'
```

Manual smoke: install hooks in a temporary HOME/config directory and verify generated config, sidecar event, and materialized archive event.
MD
cd /mnt/data && zip -r polylogue_static_bead_packets.zip polylogue_static_bead_packets >/tmp/zip2.out && ls -lh /mnt/data/polylogue_static_bead_packets.zip /mnt/data/polylogue_static_bead_packets/critical_path_packets.md
